{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"China's 'aircraft-carrier killer' missiles successfully hit a ship during recent test, Chinese insider says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/chinas-aircraft-carrier-killer-missiles-reportedly-hit-ship-in-test-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cc1cc53b14bf45ad6197666?format=jpeg\" alt=\"China military DF-26 ballistic missile Tiananmen Gate\" height=\"700\" width=\"1400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Military vehicles with DF-26 ballistic missiles in a military parade for the 70th anniversary of the end of World War II, in Beijing, September 3, 2015.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andy Wong/Pool via REUTERS</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li data-v-d2611f88=\"\">DF-26B and DF-21D missiles launched in August struck a moving vessel close to the Paracel Islands, according to former Chinese Senior Col. Wang Xiangsui.</li>\n<li data-v-d2611f88=\"\">The test \"is a warning to the US, asking it not to take any military risk,\" Wang, now a professor at Beihang University in Beijing, said at a recent event.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The two \"<a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/military/article/3098972/chinese-military-launches-two-missiles-south-china-sea-warning\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">aircraft-carrier killer</a>\" missiles that China launched in August travelled thousands of kilometres and hit their designated target, a moving ship, near the Paracel Islands in the South China Sea, according to a Chinese military expert.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">This is the first time the Chinese side has revealed details of the missile launches, which were first reported by the South China Morning Post in August. The news was later confirmed by the US military.</p><p>After the launches it was reported that the missiles fell into the <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/topics/south-china-sea\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">South China Sea</a>, but Wang Xiangsui, a former senior colonel who now works as a professor at Beihang University in Beijing, said they hit a ship, their intended target.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">One of the missiles, a DF-26B, was launched from the northwestern province of Qinghai, while the other, a DF-21D, lifted off from Zhejiang province in China's east.</p><p>The launches came a day after Beijing said a US <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/military/article/3098885/us-spy-plane-enters-no-fly-zone-during-chinese-live-fire-naval\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">U-2 spy plane entered a no-fly zone</a> without permission during a Chinese live-fire naval drill in the Bohai Sea off its northern coast. The US Navy had earlier sent two aircraft carrier strike groups into the South China Sea.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">\"So several days later [after the aircraft carrier manoeuvres], we launched the DF-21 and DF-26, and the missiles hit a vessel sailing south of the Paracel Islands,\" Wang said at a closed-door meeting in Zhejiang last month. The details of his speech were published for the first time on Wednesday.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\"></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2986e1c741f0019ac9f36?format=jpeg\" alt=\"China military missile DF-21\" height=\"1673\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A military vehicle carries DF-21D missile past an image of the Great Wall of China, in Beijing&#39;s Tiananmen Square, September 3, 2015.\n<p class=\"copyright\">GREG BAKER/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">\"Shortly after that, an American military attach√© in Geneva complained [to us] and said it would lead to severe consequences if the missiles hit an American aircraft carrier. They see this as a show of force. But we are doing this because of their provocation,\" Wang said.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">His remarks were made during the four-day Moganshan forum to discuss domestic and international issues and China's new five-year plan. The event was organised by the <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/topics/national-development-and-reform-commission\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">National Development and Reform Commission</a> and attended by 80 economists, former government officials and entrepreneurs.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">\"This is a warning to the US, asking it not to take any military risks,\" Wang said. \"Such actions mark the bottom line of Sino-US confrontation.\"</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">The missile launches came at a time of high tensions between Beijing and Washington over the disputed South China Sea.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">The US Navy said on July 4 it had deployed two aircraft carrier groups, led by the USS Nimitz and USS Ronald Reagan, to conduct tactical air defence exercises in the disputed waters \"in support of a free and open Indo-Pacific.\"</p><p>Beijing blasted the manoeuvres, describing them as <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3092661/beijing-blasts-us-over-provocative-military-acts-south-china\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">provocative</a>, while the US said China's missile launches were reckless and destabilising.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">Song Zhongping, a former instructor with the People's Liberation Army's Second Artillery Corps, said the mission was evidence that China could carry out long-range precision strikes against medium to large surface vessels.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">\"To hit a moving object is not an easy task, especially for ballistic missiles, which normally hit a stationary target,\" he said. \"The mission shows Chinese missiles are a real deterrent against US warships.\"</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">Michael Raska, an assistant professor at the S. Rajaratnam School of International Studies at Nanyang Technological University in Singapore, said China was developing advanced combat systems capable of negating the United States' traditional military superiority.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">\"The key problem for the US is to sustain its long-term deterrence, particularly in contested areas, while simultaneously mitigating risks,\" he said.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">According to a report published by the US defence department in September, <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/article/3099809/china-may-outmatch-american-military-missile-development-and\" data-v-65124bae=\"\">China may have already overtaken America</a> in the area of missile development and shipbuilding, and is set to double its nuclear warhead stockpile over the next decade.</p><p data-v-d2611f88=\"\" data-v-c48a956a=\"\">The PLA has more than 1,250 ground-launched ballistic missiles and ground-launched cruise missiles with ranges of up to 5,500 km (3,400 miles). The US has a single type of conventional ground-launched ballistic missile, with a range of 70 km to 300 km, the report said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Former President Barack Obama said he was troubled to witness Republican lawmakers doing \"a complete 180 on everything they claimed to believe\" in recent years.&#160;&#160;</li>\n<li>Obama told The Atlantic he wasn't surprised by the behavior of President Donald Trump during his time in office.&#160;</li>\n<li>But he said he was shocked to see Republicans position themselves as staunch Trump allies despite much of the president's rhetoric and actions that break with the values of the party.</li>\n<li>\"I did not believe how easily the not shocked by President Donald Trump's \"character and behavior\" while in office, but he was surprised to see Republican lawmakers doing \"a complete 180 on everything they claimed to believe.\"&#160;</p><p>In an interview with <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2020/11/why-obama-fears-for-our-democracy/617087/\">The Atlantic</a>, Obama said Trump exhibited the same values and behavior in the four years of his presidency as he did during his campaign.&#160;</p><p>Those signs were \"all evident before the 2016 election,\" Obama said. \"I didn't expect him to significantly change.\"</p><p>But Obama was surprised that some longtime Republican senators displayed a staunch loyalty to Trump, even if it meant going against their party's values.&#160;</p><p>\"I did not believe how easily the Republican establishment, people who had been in Washington for a long time and had professed a belief in certain institutional values and norms, would just cave,\" he said in the interview.&#160;</p><p>The Atlantic's Jeffrey Goldberg asked Obama about the \"complicity\" of powerhouse Sens. Lindsey Graham and Marco Rubio, two Republicans who appear to have turned into Trump loyalists.</p><p>Rubio has attended <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/marco-rubio-attends-trump-rally-michael-barbaro-2019-6\">Trump campaign rallies</a> in support of the president's reelection bid. But throughout 2016, Rubio slammed Trump for using <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/marco-rubio-donald-trump-chicago-protests-rally-2016-3\">violent language</a> and called him a \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/marco-rubio-donald-trump-con-artist-debate-2016-2\">con artist</a>.\"</p><p>In the middle of Trump's presidency, Graham became <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-lindsey-graham-and-trump-are-best-friends-2017-12\">one of his closest allies</a>. But the South Carolina senator didn't always feel warm toward Trump.</p><p lang=\"en\" data-aria-label-part=\"4\">\"I think he's a kook,\"&#160;<a href=\"https://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/lindsey-graham-trump-kook_us_5a20bf36e4b03c44072c68d5?ncid=inblnkushpmg00000009\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"0db83ebda726bddd626dbadf5146df70\">Graham said in</a>&#160;February 2016. \"I think he's crazy. I think he's unfit for office.\"</p><p lang=\"en\" data-aria-label-part=\"4\">Both Graham and Rubio vehemently opposed Trump's impeachment in 2019. Graham told CNN he'd do \"<a href=\"https://africa.businessinsider.com/politics/lindsey-graham-says-trumps-impeachment-trial-will-die-quickly-in-the-senate/jxm1nbm\">everything</a>\" in his power to make sure Trump's impeachment trial would \"die quickly.\" Rubio called it a \"<a href=\"https://medium.com/@SenatorMarcoRubio/my-statement-on-the-presidents-impeachment-trial-9669e82ccb43\">partisan impeachment</a>\" brought on by the Democrat-led House.</p><p lang=\"en\" data-aria-label-part=\"4\">Obama said that allegiance from Graham, Rubio, and other Republican lawmakers surprised him.&#160;</p><p>\"You think about John McCain: For all my differences with him, you would not have seen John McCain excuse a president cozying up to Vladimir Putin, or preferring Russian interpretations of events over those of his own intelligence agencies,\" Obama said. \"And to see figures in the Republican Party do a complete 180 on everything they claimed to believe previously is troubling.\"</p><p>Trump in 2017 said he <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-i-really-believe-putin-when-he-tells-me-russia-didnt-interfere-in-the-election-2017-11\">believed Russian President Vladimir Putin's</a> claim that Russia didn't interfere in the 2016 presidential election. Putin's statement fell entirely out of line with US intelligence reports that concluded the opposite.&#160;</p><p>Top Republicans also went against US intelligence reports, latching onto and promoting a conspiracy theory that said <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/putin-gloats-republicans-push-conspiracy-theory-ukraine-2016-2019-11\">Ukraine</a> ‚Äî not Russia ‚Äî interfered in the election.&#160;</p><p>\"Essentially what Republican elected officials have done is to say to themselves that in order to survive, we have to go along with conspiracy theorizing, false assertion, fantasies that Donald Trump and Rush Limbaugh and others in that echo chamber have concocted, because people believe them,\" Obama said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Moderna's promising coronavirus vaccine is a major beneficiary of the Trump administration's Operation Warp Speed","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-vaccine-trial-was-part-of-trump-operation-warp-speed-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb28cef1c741f0019ac9ef0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna vaccine\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>University of Miami Miller School of Medicine lab tech Sendy Puerto processes blood samples from study participants in the specimen processing labÔøº, Wednesday, Sept. 2, 2020 in Miami. The volunteers are taking part in testing the NIH funded Moderna COVID-19 vaccine.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Taimy Alvarez/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Biotechnology firm Moderna announced promising results from clinical trials of its COVID-19 vaccine candidate on Monday, with its vaccine showing 94.5% efficacy in preventing COVID-19 infections.&#160;</li>\n<li>Moderna is a major beneficiary of federal government funds through Operation Warp Speed, the Trump administration's project to fast-track the development of COVID-19 vaccines and therapeutics.&#160;</li>\n<li>The federal government granted Moderna nearly $1 billion to develop its vaccine and committed to pay $1.5 billion to buy, manufacture, and distribute the first 100 million doses with the option to buy more.&#160;</li>\n<li>Pharmaceutical giant Pfizer also conducted a successful COVID-19 vaccine trial with over 90% efficacy in partnership with German firm BioNtech, the company announced on November 9.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Biotechnology firm Moderna, a major beneficiary of US government funds through Operation Warp Speed, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">announced on Monday</a> that it conducted a successful trial of its COVID-19 vaccine candidate mRNA-1273, reporting that the vaccine <a href=\"https://www.nih.gov/news-events/news-releases/promising-interim-results-clinical-trial-nih-moderna-covid-19-vaccine\">was 94.5% effective</a>&#160;in preventing COVID-19 infections.</p><p>Moderna could receive up to $2.45 billion in federal government funds towards both vaccine development and future distribution of the vaccine if it is approved, <a href=\"https://www.hhs.gov/coronavirus/explaining-operation-warp-speed/index.html\">according to a fact sheet from the Department of Health and Human Services.</a></p><p>HHS granted Moderna $955 million to support the clinical development of its vaccine candidate. $483 million was granted when Moderna began Phase 1 trials in mid-March and another $472 million was granted to support Phase 3 of the vaccine trial in July.</p><p>In August, the federal government <a href=\"https://www.hhs.gov/coronavirus/explaining-operation-warp-speed/index.html\">also signed a $1.5 billion agreement</a> to buy and fund the distribution of the initial 100 million doses of the Moderna vaccine if it's approved, with the option to acquire more doses.</p><p>Moderna <a href=\"https://www.nih.gov/news-events/news-releases/promising-interim-results-clinical-trial-nih-moderna-covid-19-vaccine\">worked with federal researchers</a> at the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases to develop the vaccine, and the government helped design the company's trial as well.&#160;</p><p>The results of Moderna's trial comes after pharmaceutical giant Pfizer <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-to-know-about-modernas-effective-coronavirus-vaccine-2020-11\">announced on November 9</a> that it, in a partnership with German firm BioNTech, had conducted a successful vaccine trial with over 90% efficacy in preventing COVID-19.</p><p>Moderna's vaccine candidate has an advantage over Pfizer's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-temperature-stored-in-standard-refrigerator-2020-11\">in that it can be stored in a regular refrigerator</a>, while Pfizer's vaccine must be stored in a special freezer kept at -70 degrees Celsius or -94 degrees Fahrenheit ‚Äî a requirement that could hamper efforts to successfully distribute it.&#160;</p><p>Moderna's CEO Stephane Bancel praised both vaccine candidates <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-ceo-coronavirus-vaccine-timeline-when-will-i-get-a-shot-2020-11\">in an interview with Business Insider's Andrew Dunn</a>, saying that if they receive the emergency-use authorization they are seeking from the FDA, doses of both vaccines could be available on a very limited basis by the end of 2020 and broadly available to the general public by early summer 2021.&#160;</p><p>\"Another Vaccine just announced. This time by Moderna, 95% effective. For those great \"historians\", please remember that these great discoveries, which will end the China Plague, all took place on my watch!,\" <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1328341927641681922\">President Donald Trump tweeted</a> after the news broke on Monday morning.</p><p>When Pfizer announced the results of its trial, however, Trump <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/11/11/trump-angry-about-pfizer-vaccine/\">baselessly accused the FDA</a> of deliberately sitting on the positive vaccine trial news until after Election Day in order to undermine his presidential reelection campaign, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">which he resoundingly lost</a>, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/ap-fact-check-joe-biden-donald-trump-politics-coronavirus-pandemic-76d1580f82b1586b207990396c1e3b5f\">and he misrepresented the company's participation in Operation Warp Speed</a> in a subsequent press conference.&#160;</p><p>Unlike Moderna, Pfizer opted not to take federal government funds to develop the vaccine itself. But in July, <a href=\"https://www.hhs.gov/coronavirus/explaining-operation-warp-speed/index.html\">according to HHS,</a> Pfizer signed a $1.95 billion agreement with the federal government for the government to own the first 100 million doses of its vaccine and cover the costs of manufacturing and delivering those doses, if the vaccine candidate eventually receives emergency-use authorization from the Food &#38; Drug Administration.&#160;</p><p>Operation Warp Speed <a href=\"https://www.hhs.gov/coronavirus/explaining-operation-warp-speed/index.html\">has also granted US government funds</a> to support the clinical development of COVID-19 vaccine candidates in the trial stage from AstraZeneca, which is partnering with Oxford University, Johnson &#38; Johnson, and Novavax. The project has also funded COVID-19 therapeutics developed by Regegernon and Eli Lilly, both of which have received emergency use authorization from the FDA.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the vaccine","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-origins-ceo-cofounder-interviews-and-inside-the-lab-2020-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ec8369c4dca680cac322a42?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna CEO Stephane Bancel\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Moderna CEO Stephane Bancel attends a meeting with President Donald Trump, members of the Coronavirus Task Force, and pharmaceutical executives in the Cabinet Room of the White House on March 2, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Harnik/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In its short corporate history, Moderna has grown accustomed to breaking records.</p><p>A $450 million funding round in 2015 was a record for the biotech industry. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mrna-stock\">Moderna</a> raised even more the next year. And its 2018 initial public offering was the largest-ever for a biotech, raking in $564 million at a valuation exceeding $8 billion.</p><p>Then, this year, the coronavirus struck. Moderna lapped the drug industry in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-startup-to-biotech-developing-coronavirus-vaccine-flagship-pioneering-2020-5\">speedily crafting a coronavirus vaccine</a> candidate, zooming past competitors that dwarf the company in size and resources. Moderna's experimental serum was the first to begin human testing in mid-March.</p><p>The drug-industry giant Pfizer has since caught up to Moderna, and was the first to share results showing that its experimental vaccine works to prevent COVID-19, the disease caused by the coronavirus.</p><p>Moderna announced the success of its shot, which is easier to transport and store, a week after Pfizer. At first, supplies will be very limited, and there's likely to be enough demand for both shots if they're approved by regulators.</p><p>The hopes of a coronavirus vaccine that can halt the pandemic has swelled Moderna's valuation to almost $40 billion. If the company's shot is approved, it would be Moderna's first therapeutic to reach the market.</p><p>And it would be a major validation for the unproven technology Moderna used to create the shot, known as messenger RNA. Moderna's future rests on the success or failure of this platform, which the company has been working on for a decade.</p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-startup-to-biotech-developing-coronavirus-vaccine-flagship-pioneering-2020-5\">exclusive interviews</a>, Business Insider talked to CEO Stephane Bancel, cofounders Noubar Afeyan and Robert Langer, and more, about the founding of Moderna and how the company reached this pivotal moment.</p><h2><strong>Subscribe now to read our feature: Everything is gold-plated. That insinuates itself and seeps into the culture.\"</p><p>Recalling discussions with former First Lady Michelle Obama, the former president said their upbringing in middle class backgrounds meant they \"weren't subject day-to-day to the sense that if you don't have this stuff then you are somehow not worthy.\"</p><p>\"America has always had a caste system‚Äîrich and poor, not just racially but economically‚Äîbut it wasn't in your face most of the time when I was growing up,\" Obama said. \"Then you start seeing Lifestyles of the Rich and Famous, that sense that either you've got it or you're a loser. And Donald Trump epitomizes that cultural movement that is deeply ingrained now in American culture.\"</p><p>Another reason Trump's rise caught Obama by surprise was his outsize presence on television, particularly stemming from his time hosting NBC's \"The Apprentice.\"</p><p>\"I think that indicates the power of television in the culture that sometimes I miss because I don't watch a lot of TV,\" Obama said. \"I certainly don't watch reality shows.\"</p><p>\"And sometimes I'd miss things that were phenomena. But I thought there was a shift there.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a buckets.&#160;</p><p>On Monday, the chicken chain announced it will re-release its 1966 and 1971 US holiday buckets, as well as debut a vintage-inspired 2020 design. The 1966 and 1971 buckets were precisely recreated, with the '66 bucket featuring KFC's retired tagline: \"\"North America's Hospitality Dish.\"&#160;</p><p>The holiday buckets will be available in all US KFC locations starting on November 24. The company said in a press release that KFC will only provide a limited supply of the 1966 and 1971 buckets.&#160;</p><p>\"KFC bucket meals have been bringing people together around the dinner table for more than 60 years,\" said Andrea Zahumensky, KFC's US CMO, said in a statement.</p><p>\"Even though the holidays may look a little different this year, we hope our holiday buckets help everyone hark back to a simpler time and bring some comfort and joy to your homes and your families throughout the season,\" Zahumensky continued.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb28c2a1c741f0019ac9eed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Decades of Deliciousness\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>KFC has been releasing holiday buckets for years.\n<p class=\"copyright\">KFC</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>KFC is far from the only brand tapping into nostalgia in 2020.</p><p>Business Insider's Tanya Dua reported in October that brands are relying on nostalgia marketing, as people crave comfort during the pandemic. competitive. PR agencies are hiring to meet <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crisis-pr-business-surges-following-coronavirus-outbreak-2020-4\">increased demand for crisis help</a> and experts to staff healthcare, pharma, and tech accounts.</p><p>Business Insider spoke with recruiters, insiders and experts at the leading PR and strategic communications firms including Publicis' Kekst CNC and Edelman about what it takes to get hired there.&#160;</p><h2>How to get hired</h2><p>Firms like WPP's Finsbury, Kekst, and Gladstone Place Partners have carved out a lucrative but little understood industry within public relations, working on high-stakes crises like WeWork's downward spiral and blockbuster mergers like Disney-Fox.</p><p>The pay can be lucrative, but the tradeoff is that people have to thrive under pressure and have a high tolerance for long hours.</p><p><strong>Read about strategic consulting firms: </strong><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-get-job-at-finsbury-gladstone-place-partners-kekst-2020-9\">How to get hired at strategic consulting firms, where junior staffers can start out making $95,000</a></strong></p><p>Publicis-owned Kekst CNC, one of the most prestigious public relations firms, pioneered a new space for PR in advising on mergers and financial crises.</p><p>It uses interviews with employees at different seniority levels and a writing test to assess candidates' empathy and judgement.</p><p>Candidates also get a test presenting a made-up situation like a crisis, earnings call, announcement, along with some data, requiring them to draft a response or communications plan.</p><p><strong>Go deeper: </strong><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kekst-cnc-reveals-details-of-its-interview-process-2020-9\">How to get a job at Publicis Groupe's Kekst CNC, the PR firm behind some of the biggest deals in the world, according to hiring execs there</a></strong></p><p>Strategic communications firms like WPP's Finsbury and Gladstone Place Partners seek people who thrive under pressure and use the interview process to test job candidates' intellectual curiosity, commitment to their job, and if they're good fits.</p><p>Current and former employees at these and other firms shared the toughest questions candidates can expect, which can include deceptively simple ones like \"Why are you interviewing for a job here?\" and head-scratching riddles.</p><p><strong>Read more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/toughest-interview-questions-at-wpps-finsbury-publicis-kekst-cnc-2020-9\">Tricky job interview questions to expect at strategic PR firms like WPP's Finsbury and Publicis' Kekst CNC, according to insiders</a></strong></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/22-power-players-at-edelman-the-worlds-largest-pr-firm-2020-8\">Worldwide PR firm Edelman</a> is highly competitive, with its US offices having gotten more than 4,000 job applications per month for an average of 175 openings.</p><p>Recruiters gave tips on how to land a job and get ready for an interview, by researching company culture, preparing to talk about your mistakes, and more.</p><p>One tip: Edelman doesn't ask for cover letters and looks for people who aren't on the job market, so having a current LinkedIn page is crucial.&#160;<br>&#160;<br><strong>Read about interviewing at Edelman: </strong><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-get-a-job-at-public-relations-giant-edelman-2020-2\">How to get a job at PR giant Edelman and what to expect if you land an interview, according to the company's recruiters</a></strong></p><h2>What PR jobs pay</h2><p>Around 270,000 people worked as PR specialists in the US as of 2019, according to the Bureau of Labor Statistics.</p><p>Business Insider analyzed government data for the largest independent and holding company-owned PR firms and found salaries range from $62,000 for a senior account executive at finance-focused Prosek Partners to $420,000 for a managing director at consulting firm FTI Consulting.</p><p><strong>Learn about PR salaries: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pr-industry-salaries-edelman-apco-worldwide-omnicom-wpp-publicis-teneo-2020-8\">PR industry salaries revealed: How much top firms like Teneo, BCW, and FTI pay employees, from consultants to managing directors</a></strong></p><h2>Hiring trends to know</h2><p>Pandemic-related layoffs have given public relations employers a hiring edge for the first time in years and made PR recruiters, a vital link between employers and candidates, even more critical.</p><p>Business Insider identified a dozen leading PR headhunters, including two in-house recruiters.</p><p>Among the trends they're seeing: clients are hiring to staff growing areas of healthcare, pharma, and tech PR; diverse candidates are in high demand; and brands are hiring more than agencies.</p><p>They also said good internal communications experts are in demand as companies look at to stay connected with their remote employees.</p><p><strong>What leading headhunters say: </strong><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/12-top-public-relations-recruiters-to-know-right-now-2020-7\">Meet 12 top public relations recruiters to know right One asked if Amazon could give Scotland independence from the UK.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Amazon apologized Saturday after its official support Twitter account repeatedly insisted, incorrectly, that Northern Ireland wasn't part of the UK.</p><p>The tech giant's apology came four hours after a customer, who recently moved from the Republic of Ireland to Northern Ireland, complained that he couldn't watch live rugby on Amazon Prime.</p><p>In response to the complaint, Amazon Help said: \"We apologize but upon reviewing your location you're in Northern Ireland. Rugby Autumn Nations Cup coverage is exclusively available to Prime members based in the UK. We don't have the rights to other territories.\"</p><p>Even when Twitter users highlighted the geographical mistake, Amazon Help continued to insist that the company doesn't have rights to Northern Ireland because it's outside the UK.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Amazon Help  (@AmazonHelp) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1327696870454517762?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 14, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Four hours later, the account apologized, and said that Amazon Prime subscribers in Northern Ireland and the rest of the UK can watch the Rugby Autumn Nations Cup.</p><p>\"We apologise for the error in our colleague's response. Our Prime Video subscribers in Northern Ireland and the rest of the UK can access and watch the Rugby Autumn Nations Cup on Prime Video as part of their subscription.\"</p><blockquote (Kate Duffy)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f584dc87ed0ee001e25e1b1?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn87@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-786_02bee5ef5a817542.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=MCqqVVERFtM:Mpohfx0Fy-Y:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn23@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-46-25-813_c56bf81795390bf5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=MCqqVVERFtM:Mpohfx0Fy-Y:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn4@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-46-24-059_37c6703b60e98a17.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=MCqqVVERFtM:Mpohfx0Fy-Y:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn68@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-25-518_ac02718246faab07.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/MCqqVVERFtM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn48@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-29-027_c07b0c4a9137e49e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138318},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"THEN AND NOW: How fast-food menus have changed over the years","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/then-and-now-how-fast-food-menus-have-changed-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae7ff58c24d0a566dde35?format=jpeg\" alt=\"In-N-Out vintage\" height=\"975\" width=\"1300\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In-N-Out in the 1960s.\n<p class=\"copyright\">In-N-Out</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>McDonald's Big Mac, Burger King's Whopper, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/popeyes-chicken-sandwich-steals-crown-from-chick-fil-a-2019-11\">Popeyes' chicken sandwich</a> &#8212; while these items are now undeniably iconic, at one point they were all brand new.</li>\n<li><strong>Business Insider looked at how <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/then-and-now-mcdonalds-menu-items-2020-2\">fast-food restaurant menus</a> have changed over the years, from McDonald's to Chick-fil-A to In-N-Out.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Some menu changes brought about astronomical sales, while <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fast-food-menu-changes-outraged-customers-2020-8\">others outraged customers</a> to the point of social media rants and even violence.</strong></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>When the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-mcdonalds-was-like-1950s-2020-7\">McDonald brothers opened</a> their first restaurant in 1940, it served barbecue food, while Taco Bell's first location had just five items on the menu. But over time, these restaurants have perfected their offerings, ultimately becoming the fast-food giants we know today.</p><p>Business Insider took a look back at how the menus at McDonald's, Burger King, Chick-fil-A, In-N-Out, White Castle, Taco Bell, and Popeyes have evolved over time.</p><p>Here's how fast-food menus have changed over the years.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tWhen the McDonald brothers opened their first restaurant, it served barbecue food.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f03485d4dca684f012b0834?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mcdonalds vintage\" height=\"3809\" width=\"5079\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The exterior of a McDonald&#39;s drive-in fast-food restaurant, which advertises 15-cent hamburgers, Chicago, Illinois.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hulton Archive/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>At the original McDonald's Bar-B-Q restaurant in San Bernardino, California, customers could pull up to the restaurant for carhop service. Future locations would switch to the walk-up model to order from the restaurant's large menu.</p>\n\tIn 1948, the McDonald brothers reduced the restaurant's offerings down to just nine items to make their Speedee Service system even more efficient.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2b16d4f0f4191e704f189a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"first mcdonalds museum\" height=\"1782\" width=\"2376\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tim Boyle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/then-and-now-mcdonalds-menu-items-2020-2\">new menu</a> included hamburgers, cheeseburgers, soft drinks, milk, coffee, potato chips, and a slice of pie for dessert. In 1949, potato chips were swapped with french fries and McDonald's began selling milkshakes.</p>\n\tThe addition of milkshakes to the McDonald's menu in 1949 would completely shift the future of the chain.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f0382694dca68693d4f3295?format=jpeg\" alt=\"first mcdonalds museum\" height=\"1596\" width=\"2128\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s milkshake cups in the McDonald&#39;s museum.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ralf-Finn Hestoft/Corbis/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The new item, called Triple Thick Milkshakes, was made using Multimixer.</p><p>After Multimixer salesman&#160;<a href=\"https://corporate.mcdonalds.com/corpmcd/about-us/history.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\">Ray Kroc visited the original McDonald's brothers</a> to sell them more mixers, he became intrigued in the business. He would go on to purchase the small business and become the tycoon and leader of the fast-food giant for 30 years.</p><p>Today, McDonald's still serves milkshakes, as well as McFlurries.</p>\n\tIn 1965, McDonald's introduced the Filet-O-Fish sandwich nationwide.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae43028ea710c964dc606?format=jpeg\" alt=\"filet o fish mcdonald&#39;s\" height=\"1426\" width=\"1901\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An ad for the Filet-O-Fish.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mike Blake/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>According to <a href=\"https://www.smithsonianmag.com/arts-culture/the-fishy-history-of-the-mcdonalds-filet-o-fish-sandwich-2912/\">Smithsonian Magazine</a>, it was created in 1962 by Lou Groen, a McDonald's franchise owner in Cincinnati, Ohio, after he realized hamburger sales were declining on Fridays during the season of Lent.</p><p>Groen then decided to create a sandwich featuring fish instead of beef. Three years later, it was made available nationwide and has remained on McDonald's menus ever since.</p>\n\tMcDonald's added the now-iconic Big Mac to its menu in 1967.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae3ea2618b933c60ebe9c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"big mac 1977\" height=\"1579\" width=\"2105\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Product shot of a McDonald&#39;s Big Mac hamburger in 1977.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Henry Groskinsky/The LIFE Images Collection/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The first \"Big Mac\" featured a triple-decker burger and sold for 45 cents.&#160;</p><p>Initially, there was a lot of deliberation over <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-the-mcdonalds-big-mac-got-its-name\">what the iconic burger would be named</a>. However, Esther Glickstein Rose, a 21-year-old secretary for the company's advertising department in 1967, had the winning name &#8212; \"Big Mac.\" Despite the name originally being ridiculed, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/4338738fbc4ed82ddfcd5700c17d6ebd\">according to AP</a>, it's now known as one of \"the best-known product names of all time.\"</p>\n\tChicken McNuggets were added to menus in 1983.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae5741918242f7b02b5f3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"McDonald&#39;s Chicken Nuggets\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s Chicken McNuggets.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Irene Jiang / Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>According to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/food/2018/03/13/mcdonalds-debuted-happy-meal-39-years-ago-heres-how-its-changed/419395002/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\">USA Today</a>, many diners in the 1980s were looking to reduce their fat intake and were shaking up their diets by introducing more lean protein and poultry and cutting out red meat. For McDonald's, adding chicken to their menu was a no-brainer.</p><p>This year, McDonald's added a spicy version of its chicken nuggets to menus. They quickly sold out and are no longer available in most locations.</p>\n\tAs a result of the coronavirus pandemic and trying to streamline its operations, McDonald's is now offering a limited menu.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae37aaee6a80ccb26802e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"coronavirus mcdonalds menu\" height=\"2376\" width=\"3167\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s drive-through during the coronavirus pandemic.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Ross D. Franklin</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>McDonald's&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-mcdonalds-cuts-back-on-menu-ends-all-day-breakfast-2020-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\">stopped serving all-day breakfast</a> and removed its chicken tenders, grilled chicken sandwich, a few burgers, and salads from menus nationwide.</p><p>\"To simplify operations in our kitchens and for our crew, and ensure the best possible experience for our customers, we are working with our franchisees and local restaurants to focus on serving our most popular choices and will begin temporarily removing some items from the menu,\" Bill Garrett, McDonald's senior vice president of operations,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-mcdonalds-cuts-back-on-menu-ends-all-day-breakfast-2020-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\">said in a statement to Business Insider</a>.</p><p>While some items, like the Bacon McDouble, are back, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fast-food-menu-items-you-will-never-order-again-2020-8\">others have been permanently cut from the menu</a>.</p>\n\tMcDonald's is also experimenting with celebrity collaborations in a bid to reach Gen Z customers.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeb34d1c741f0019ac9a76?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Travis Scott\" height=\"1742\" width=\"2322\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Travis Scott surprises crew and customers at McDonald&#39;s for the launch of the Travis Scott Meal on September 08, 2020, in Downey, California.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jerritt Clark/Getty Images for McDonald&#39;s</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Rapper Travis Scott's collaboration with the chain was a huge success &#8212; so much so that McDonald's reported it was experiencing burger shortages as people clamored to try it. About a month after the release of the Travis Scott meal collab, McDonald's launched another partnership with reggaeton star J Balvin.</p><p>Neither meals included new menu items, showing <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-teams-up-with-j-balvin-in-latest-celebrity-partnership-2020-10\">the power of celebrity to inspire younger customers to order from McDonald's</a>.</p>\n\tMcDonald's is also prepping to bring back some fan-favorite, nostalgic menu items.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeb73a1c741f0019ac9a90?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mcrib\" height=\"1547\" width=\"2062\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s McRib.\n<p class=\"copyright\">PAUL J. RICHARDS/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The infamous McRib sandwich first appeared on McDonald's menus in 1981. After four years of lackluster sales,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.mentalfloss.com/article/29134/10-meaty-facts-about-mcrib\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"bd4d7974293e2ecc53eafb77e915ccbb\">it was removed from the chain's menu</a>. However, in 1989, the McRib returned. Until 2005, the item could be found on many McDonald's menus worldwide and is&#160;<a href=\"https://independenttravelcats.com/mcrib-germany/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"7b77a0d820e4813046c887c14f7641ff\">a staple at locations in Germany and Luxembourg</a>.&#160;</p><p>In 2012, the McRib made its return to some menus after years of fan requests. However, just as quickly as it came, it disappeared. Now, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-mcrib-to-return-nationally-in-2020-sparking-celebration-2020-10\">McDonald's has announced the McRib will be available nationwide once again on December 2</a>.</p>\n\tPlant-based menu items could be the future of McDonald's.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faebaf61c741f0019ac9ab3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mcdonald&#39;s plt\" height=\"976\" width=\"1301\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>McDonald&#39;s PLT.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.mcdonalds.com/ca/en-ca/local/plt.html?cid=web:ca-redirect:all:press-release-plt:na:na\" target=\"_blank\">McDonald&#39;s</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>On November 9, McDonald's announced it would officially be venturing into the world of plant-based meat products. The chain is now in the process of developing the \"McPlant,\" a lineup of plant-based burgers, \"chicken,\" and more meat-free menu items, according to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcplants-name-reveals-mcdonalds-takes-plant-based-meat-seriously-2020-11\">Business Insider</a>.</p><p>McDonald's previously tested a plant-based burger called the PLT in Canada using Beyond Meat. Now, the fast-food powerhouse is setting its sights on creating its own meat substitute crafted exclusively for McDonald's restaurants.</p><p>\"It's not a matter of if McDonald's will get into plant-based,\" CEO Chris Kempczinski said, according to Business Insider. \"It's a matter of when.\"</p>\n\tBurger King opened its doors in Jacksonville, Florida, in 1953, as \"Insta-Burger King.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae94440c1f37f9d07aad3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Burger King\" height=\"1091\" width=\"1454\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An early Burger King restaurant.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/burgerking/photos/pb.134615383218473.-2207520000.1454005909./577901862223154/?type=3&#38;theater\" target=\"_blank\">Burger King Facebook</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The chain, which quickly grew to be the second-largest fast-food chain in the country, behind McDonald's, served 18-cent flame-broiled burgers, milkshakes, and fries.</p>\n\tIn 1957, Burger King released its signature burger, the Whopper.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f282e157924a1160b3aabb7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"burger king whopper \" height=\"2360\" width=\"3147\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Burger King Whopper.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The&#160;<a href=\"https://www.encyclopedia.com/social-sciences-and-law/economics-business-and-labor/businesses-and-occupations/burger-king-corp#1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\">Whopper was 37 cents</a>&#160;compared to Burger King's original burger, which cost 18 cents. The Whopper came with sauce, cheese, lettuce, pickles, and tomato, all piled on top of a larger patty.</p><p>Today, Burger King&#160;still broils and flame-grills its burgers.</p>\n\tMore recently, Burger King revolutionized its menu with the addition of the Impossible Whopper, a meat-free version of its iconic sandwich.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae9e15af6cc037c3e5d76?format=jpeg\" alt=\"burger king menu impossible whopper\" height=\"683\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Close-up of Burger King menu board with an advertisement for the Impossible Whopper.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Smith Collection/Gado/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Burger King's Impossible Whopper was hugely successful for the chain. According to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2019/10/28/investing/restaurant-brands-earnings-burger-king-popeyes/index.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\">CNN</a>, Burger King reported a 10% increase in sales following the launch of the Impossible Burger in 2019.</p><p>However, while the burger is plant-based, Burger King received criticism after a customer sued the company for serving the burger that's not actually 100% vegan. Since the patties are cooked on the same grills as traditional meat burgers, they may&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lawsuit-claims-burger-kings-impossible-whoppers-are-contaminated-by-meat-2019-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\">come into contact with meat by-products</a>. Burger King responded saying the chain never advertised the burger as vegan or promised to cook them in a particular way.</p>\n\tThe Dwarf Grill in Hapeville, Georgia, opened in 1946. It would eventually become what we now know as Chick-fil-A.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae6a9aee6a80e1b0d8eb7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chickfila menu\" height=\"676\" width=\"901\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dwarf Grill menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider/Hayley Peterson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The business, owned and operated by founder Truett Cathy, started off by selling standard items like waffles, breakfast foods, sandwiches, and burgers.&#160;</p>\n\tHowever, everything changed when Chick-fil-A created its original chicken sandwich in 1964.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aeb8f58c24d0af911ce05?format=jpeg\" alt=\"chick-fil-a sandwich\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chick-fil-A chicken sandwich.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shutterstock/rblfmr</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>According to Chick-fil-A, Cathy tested hundreds of recipes for the original chicken sandwich before landing on a winner &#8212; a fried chicken fillet with two pickles on a toasted butter bun.</p><p>Though Chick-fil-A has expanded immensely since then, the chicken sandwich has remained virtually the same.</p>\n\tIn 1989, Chick-fil-A added a grilled chicken sandwich to its menu.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aec3faee6a80f763fff19?format=jpeg\" alt=\"2 chick fil a grilled chicken club\" height=\"800\" width=\"1067\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chick-fil-A grilled chicken club sandwich.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hollis Johnson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Introduced as a <a href=\"https://thechickenwire.chick-fil-a.com/food/a-staple-since-1989-our-grilled-chicken-evolution\">\"health-conscious option\"</a> for Chick-fil-A customers, Cathy introduced the original grilled chicken sandwich alongside the deluxe grilled chicken sandwich, which included the same pickle-juice-marinated grilled chicken, pickles, and white bun, along with lettuce and tomato.</p><p>In 1993, Chick-fil-A added the grilled chicken club sandwich to its menu. Then, in 2017, the chain announced it would be releasing a gluten-free bun option.</p>\n\tToday, the menu has more than 40 different menu items, but you certainly won't find burgers.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aeabf3f7370469d01a006?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Chick-fil-A\" height=\"932\" width=\"1243\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chick-fil-A restaurant.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mark Lennihan/Associated Press</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The menu is continually shifting gears to appeal to customers, but the chain's most famous item is undoubtedly still its original chicken sandwich.</p>\n\tIn-N-Out became California's first drive-thru hamburger stand when it opened in 1948.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae7ff58c24d0a566dde35?format=jpeg\" alt=\"In-N-Out vintage\" height=\"975\" width=\"1300\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In-N-Out in the 1960s.\n<p class=\"copyright\">In-N-Out</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In 1958, In-N-Out replaced its bottled drinks with fountain service, offering customers beverages like Pepsi Cola, Nesbitt Orange, and Hires Root Beer. According to In-N-Out, a <a href=\"https://www.in-n-out.com/history\">12-ounce soda cost just 10 cents</a> at the time.</p>\n\tIn 1961, In-N-Out added \"animal style\" burgers to its menu.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2c29457924a13815397800?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Animal Style In-n-Out\" height=\"667\" width=\"889\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In-N-Out animal style burger.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Yelp</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The first Animal Style burger hit menus as a response to overwhelming customer requests. The recipe is still the same today as it was in the 1960s &#8212; a mustard-cooked beef patty, lettuce, tomato, pickles, extra spread, and grilled onions.</p>\n\tIn 1963, In-N-Out began serving its famous Double-Double burger.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2b0136de1e9619d97fba5a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"In n Out menu\" height=\"1613\" width=\"2150\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Double-Double burger on the menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Irene Jiang/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In 1975, In-N-Out began serving milkshakes. A few years later, In-N-Out opened its <a href=\"https://www.in-n-out.com/history\">first location with a dining room</a> in Ontario, California.</p><p>However, while some new items have been added since 1948, the menu is still pretty similar to the original menu, offering basic fast-food items like burgers and fries.</p>\n\tWhite Castle is regarded as the first fast-food hamburger chain in America. It opened its doors in 1921.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae2c74e52b70501492615?format=jpeg\" alt=\"white castle\" height=\"799\" width=\"1065\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>White Castle.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/WhiteCastle/photos_stream\" target=\"_blank\">White Castle</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.whitecastle.com/about-us/our-history\">Founded by Billy Ingram</a> as a family-owned business, the fast-food establishment originally sold 5-cent, small, square hamburgers by the sack. They would come to be known as \"sliders.\"</p><p>In 1943, <a href=\"https://www.whitecastle.com/about-us/our-history\">White Castle would sell hot dogs</a> and fried eggs instead of its iconic burgers as a result of the war's beef rationing.</p>\n\tIn 1962, White Castle began selling cheeseburgers.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2c41922618b9676d2c9a81?format=jpeg\" alt=\"white castle sliders\" height=\"683\" width=\"911\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>White Castle sliders on a grill.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Win McNamee/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>This addition came 15 years after the chain secured a patent for its <a href=\"https://www.whitecastle.com/about-us/our-history\">\"holy\" burgers</a> &#8212; each burger is still grilled with five holes punched into it to add more flavor and help them cook faster.</p>\n\tToday, White Castle still sells its iconic sliders.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae2b24e52b70501492612?format=jpeg\" alt=\"White Castle 3\" height=\"1239\" width=\"1652\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>White Castle food.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hollis Johnson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The sliders are also sold in grocery stores nationwide, meaning you can get your White Castle fix right at home. In 2018, White Castle revolutionized its menu by offering the plant-based Impossible Slider.</p>\n\tTaco Bell offered just five menu items when it opened in 1962.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae873191824308469e8d5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Taco Bell menu vintage\" height=\"746\" width=\"994\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taco Bell&#39;s original menu, with its first franchisee, Kermit Becky.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Taco Bell</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Each item cost just 19 cents, and the menu featured traditional Mexican favorites like frijoles, tostadas, burritos, and tacos.</p><p>In 1984, <a href=\"https://www.tacobell.com/history\">Taco Bell introduced the Taco Salad and Taco BellGrande</a>&#160;and, in 2004, Taco Bell began selling Mountain Dew Baja Blast.</p>\n\tIn 2014, Taco Bell officially launched its breakfast menu nationwide.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aef22a6f0e10aea31ee66?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Taco Bell Breakfast Menu 10\" height=\"990\" width=\"1321\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taco Bell breakfast burrito.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hollis Johnson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>It was the <a href=\"https://www.qsrweb.com/articles/taco-bell-plans-to-reinvent-qsr-breakfast-experience/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" data-ga-track=\"ExternalLink:https://www.qsrweb.com/articles/taco-bell-plans-to-reinvent-qsr-breakfast-experience/\" aria-label=\"brand's largest marketing campaign ever\">brand's largest marketing campaign</a> to date and has proven to be successful year over year.</p><p>However, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-needs-to-boost-breakfast-after-coronavirus-demolishes-sales-2020-4\">coronavirus pandemic has caused fast-food breakfast sales to plummet</a>, leaving the future of breakfast foods at giants like Taco Bell and McDonald's uncertain.</p>\n\tToday, Taco Bell has an expansive menu that offers a lot more than it did in the 1960s.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2ae841f34d0527d435eab7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Taco Bell menu\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2223\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taco Bell menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Irene Jiang / Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Countless different varieties of tacos and burritos make <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/taco-bell-value-menu-items-one-dollar-ranking-review\">eating the entire menu</a> a tall order.</p>\n\tHowever, the menu is getting a tad smaller.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa97636f7d1cb0019e3a8aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"taco bell cheesy fiesta potatoes\" height=\"645\" width=\"859\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Taco Bell Cheesy Fiesta Potatoes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Diana G./Yelp</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In July, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/taco-bell-cuts-menu-removing-potatoes-loaded-grillers-nachos-supreme-2020-7\">fast-food chain announced it would be removing 12 items from its menu</a>, including fan-favorite items such as Cheesy Fiesta Potatoes, Nachos Supreme, and Loaded Grillers. Some <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fast-food-menu-changes-outraged-customers-2020-8\">fans were outraged by the decision to ax potatoes</a>, calling it the chain's \"worst idea to date.\"</p><p>In September, Taco Bell announced it would be dropping the fan-favorite Mexican Pizza from its newly streamlined menu starting November 5.</p><p>\"We know some fans may be sad to see this one go, we are too. One silver lining of saying goodbye to the Mexican Pizza that might help you rest easy is that removing it from our menus helps us work towards our&#160;commitment&#160;to leave a lighter footprint on our planet,\" Taco Bell said in a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.tacobell.com/news/taco-bell-completes-2020-menu-revamp\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"bd56646aed89b021656529ff1d52b1ac\">press release</a>.</p>\n\tPopeyes first opened in 1972 as \"Chicken on the Run\" in the New Orleans suburb of Arabi, Louisiana.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aee92aee6a810322e82d2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"popeyes\" height=\"984\" width=\"1312\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Popeyes restaurant in 2000.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David McNew/Newsmakers/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The <a href=\"https://www.popeyes.com/our-story\">restaurant originally served traditional, Southern-style fried chicken</a>. However, after the restaurant faced lackluster sales for a few months, founder Alvin C. Copeland Sr. changed the restaurant's name to \"Popeyes\" and began selling spicy New Orleans-style chicken.</p>\n\tIn 1983, Popeyes began selling buttermilk biscuits.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2c47145fa9a435340683b0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Popeyes\" height=\"1299\" width=\"1732\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Popeyes restaurant.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brad Kemp / AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The biscuits are now regarded as one of Popeyes' most iconic menu items and come with the chain's combo meals.</p>\n\tBefore its famous chicken sandwich hit the menu, Popeyes mainly sold fried chicken and seafood.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aee01191824313b3582ca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"popeyes menu\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2667\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Popeyes restaurant takeout order menu is seen on February 21, 2017, in Miami, Florida.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Joe Raedle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The chain launched its Butterfly Shrimp Tackle Box <a href=\"https://www.popeyes.com/our-story\">in 2009</a>, while Chicken Waffle Tenders and the Cajun Surf &#38; Turf hit menus in 2013.&#160;</p>\n\tPopeyes changed its direction ‚Äî and, perhaps, the entire face of fast food ‚Äî when it launched its now-famous chicken sandwich in 2019.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f2aed4f5af6cc04156752fa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"popeyes chicken sandwich sold out\" height=\"683\" width=\"911\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A sign indicating that chicken sandwiches are sold out at a Boston Popeyes in 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Pat Greenhouse/The Boston Globe/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The chicken sandwich was so popular, it quickly <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/popeyes-workers-describe-chicken-sandwich-demand-chaos-2019-8\">sent restaurants into chaos</a> before selling out entirely in just two weeks. A few months later, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/popeyes-chicken-sandwich-returns-chick-fil-a-battle-2019-10\">the menu item finally returned</a>, much to the satisfaction of chicken and fast-food lovers nationwide.</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-mcdonalds-was-like-1950s-2020-7\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">This is what it was like to go to McDonald's in the 1950s</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/in-n-out-review-double-double-animal-style-fries-2019-12\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">I just went to In-N-Out for the first time in years. The burger was better than I remembered, but the fries were hugely disappointing.</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/then-and-now-mcdonalds-menu-items-2020-2\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">THEN AND NOW: How the McDonald's menu has changed through the years</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/then-and-now-mcdonalds-restaurants-through-the-years\" data-read-more-link=\"\" data-e2e-name=\"read-more-link\">THEN AND NOW: Photos show how McDonald's has changed through the years, from its menu to its mascot</a></li></ul>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"3 ways to avoid getting taken advantage of by lazy coworkers","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-for-dealing-with-lazy-unproductive-coworkers-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f243c5440c1f31ff968cded?format=jpeg\" alt=\"friends talking\" height=\"3667\" width=\"5500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If the problem persists, make your manager aware of the problem without letting anger or annoyance get in the way.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Hinterhaus Productions/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If you're constantly doing someone else's work, it's time to set boundaries and politely push back when your coworker asks you for favors.</li>\n<li>Instead of giving in, prioritize your own work and learn to be assertive or say \"no\" without getting too emotional.&#160;</li>\n<li>Avoid sounding hostile by offering guidance and suggestions that will help them complete the task at hand themselves.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Lazy coworkers are, in a word, aggravating. Part of being a <a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/teamwork-skills\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">team player</a> is pitching in and helping a colleague meet a crazy deadline, or taking on part of their workload when they need an extra hand. But that's supposed to be once in a while ‚Äî a favor, not a full-time job.</p><p>If you're constantly doing someone else's work, it can be difficult to fulfill your own responsibilities, produce high-quality work and go above and beyond. It could even be the difference between a promotion and staying stagnant.</p><p>And as helpful as you want to be, if your willingness to help turns into an everyday occurrence, you're&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/being-taken-advantage-of-at-work-0517\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">being taken advantage of</a>. It may be time to say something. \"Follow the rule of three to make sure you're dealing with a pattern and not an incident,\" said Leigh Steere, cofounder of the Boulder-based management training tool Managing People Better. \"If it happens once, let it go; twice, make a mental note; three times, you have to deal with it,\"</p><p>Monster spoke to career experts to find out how to politely (but firmly)&#160;<a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/say-no-push-back-0717\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">push back</a> on the work your coworker tries to push off.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/michael-jordan-view-winning-great-advice-business-leaders-success-2020-5\">Michael Jordan was asked if his desire to win cost him a nice-guy reputation. His emotional response is being touted as one of the best quotes on leadership.</a></em></p><h2><strong>1. Just say no</strong></h2><p>It is possible that your colleague doesn't realize the pattern she has fallen into or how it impacts you. If you've helped her out dozens of times, it makes sense that your colleague keeps swinging by your desk at 5 p.m. with a \"huge favor to ask you.\"</p><p>\"Your communication and lack of assertiveness may be to blame. Retrain that colleague to know you are no longer doing two jobs,\" said Angelina Darrisaw, founder and CEO of the New York-based career coaching firm C-Suite Coach. \"This means being willing to <a href=\"https://www.monster.com/career-advice/article/How-to-Just-Say-No\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">say 'no'&#160;</a>and 'not right now.' If you notice that your coworker always comes to you for 'help' and 'help' turns into you doing their work, start pushing back.\"</p><p>Steele advocates for being more assertive by pointing out the issue and offering a solution. She recommends telling your colleague: \"I don't mind helping every once in awhile, but I'm noticing that you are asking me to help with things from your to-do list frequently. I have a full plate without taking on more, and I need to say no.\"</p><h2><strong>2. Give guidance, not time</strong></h2><p>It is normal to want to say yes when someone asks for your help, but instead of agreeing to take the entire project ‚Äî aka hours of work ‚Äî offer to help your lazy coworker in a less time-intensive capacity.</p><p>\"Hold a brief meeting where you offer suggestions and guidance. Give them a roadmap and let them run with it. If you want, you can suggest a follow-up meeting to review the work before they turn it in,\" said Darrisaw. \"Consulting your colleague is fine, but you shouldn't be always doing the work for them.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mailchimp-set-clear-goals-key-managing-remote-teams-2020-8\">Mailchimp's chief product officer says clarifying priorities should be your number one focus when managing a 100% remote team ‚Äî here's how to start setting clear, actionable goals</a></em></p><h2><strong>3. State the facts (and leave emotion out of it)</strong></h2><p>If the problem persists even after you've talked to your colleague once or twice, you should make your manager aware of the situation.</p><p>\"Be sure to include the impact on you, such as missed deadlines, extra hours, using team resources on unscheduled projects,\" said Nancy Halpern, a coach at the New York-based executive coaching firm KNH Associates. \"But be careful of your emotions: Don't let anger or whining influence how you present. Just stick to the facts and ask your boss' advice on what else you should do to resolve it.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-for-dealing-with-lazy-unproductive-coworkers-2020-11'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
