Here's what the experience was like ‚Äî and why it's given me hope for the world.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/i-volunteered-moderna-covid-19-vaccine-trial-antibodies-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7e2908c655f6001969ecd0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elle Hardy\" height=\"2316\" width=\"3088\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elle Hardy.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Elle Hardy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Journalist Elle Hardy is taking part in a phase-three trial of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-releases-first-human-trial-results-2020-5\">Moderna's mRNA-1273</a> vaccine, which just announced it's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">94.5% effective against coronavirus</a>.</li>\n<li>The federal government announced in August that it would <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/moderna-stock-price-us-government-deal-coronavirus-vaccine-doses-trump-2020-8-1029496298#\">spend $1.53 billion to buy 100 million doses of the vaccine</a>, with an option to purchase up to 400 million additional doses.</li>\n<li>After a slight reaction to the two doses, Hardy said she was certain she didn't receive a placebo.&#160;</li>\n<li>A recent antibody test confirmed she's positive, and she thinks this is due to the vaccine.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><h2>The opportunity came my way and I didn't hesitate.</h2><p>I wish I could say that I signed up for the <a href=\"https://www.nih.gov/news-events/news-releases/phase-3-clinical-trial-investigational-vaccine-covid-19-begins\">Moderna mRNA-1273 vaccine</a> trial out of some sense of public service. But my first response when I was asked to take part in the trial was, \"Hell yes,\" because I wanted a chance to get some protection from the coronavirus as soon as possible.</p><p>My participation in the trial came about because a couple of years ago I did a medical trial for an anthrax vaccine with a company called <a href=\"https://www.benchmarkresearch.net/\">Benchmark Research</a> when I was broke. I'd completely forgotten about it, but they called me in May to say that the study was over and that I'd been given the placebo.</p><p>The doctor on the phone told me that they were finalizing an agreement for an urgent trial of a vaccine for \"you know what.\" They couldn't release information at that time, but they needed to quickly vet and enroll 30,000 subjects across multiple sites in the United States.&#160;</p><p>I jumped at it. I'd been in South Korea in February researching the <a href=\"https://foreignpolicy.com/2020/08/19/south-korea-coronavirus-scapegoat-shincheonji/\">religious group that was the source of the major outbreak</a> in the country and managed to escape infection. I returned back to my native Australia for the initial lockdown, but after a few months I needed to return to the US for work.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7e2967282c500018c793aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elle Hardy in South Korea before the pandemic\" height=\"499\" width=\"665\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Hardy in South Korea before the pandemic.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Elle Hardy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In all of my travels, I'd somehow managed to avoid getting sick (as far as I could tell), but didn't want to keep riding my luck. Coming from a country with universal healthcare, an American hospital bill terrifies me as much as contracting the virus itself.</p><h2>The science behind the vaccine is interesting.</h2><p>The Moderna vaccine isn't a live virus, but <a href=\"https://www.nationalgeographic.com/science/2020/05/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-how-it-works-cvd/#:~:text=Moderna's%20messenger%20RNA%20(mRNA)%20vaccine,it%20can%20establish%20an%20infection.\">replicates a similar immune response</a> in our bodies. It uses messenger RNA (mRNA), which is a molecule that instructs our bodies to make coronavirus spike proteins as though they'd been infected. In time, this produces antibodies in our system that look like the ones produced by people who've had the virus.</p><p>The aim of the trial is to determine whether the vaccine prevents people from catching COVID-19 or lessens the severity for people who do. The vaccine moved from the lab to human trials in a record 63 days. Early trials showed it was safe for human use, and that there were indications that it produced neutralizing antibodies in some of the patients.&#160;</p><p>I wasn't concerned about receiving an experimental drug. I knew that scientists had been researching this type of virus since the <a href=\"https://theconversation.com/the-mysterious-disappearance-of-the-first-sars-virus-and-why-we-need-a-vaccine-for-the-current-one-but-didnt-for-the-other-137583\">SARS outbreak in 2002</a>, and had <a href=\"https://www.spokesman.com/stories/2020/feb/22/by-decoding-the-coronavirus-genome-scientists-seek/\">decoded the COVID-19 genome</a> in January. In spite of political and market pressure, I can't see pharmaceutical companies blowing up their reputations by pushing forward with a vaccine that's dangerous to humans.</p><h2>The medical trial process is quite strict.</h2><p>Before I got the jab, I had to go through a lot of checks to make sure I was in good health for an experimental (at this stage) treatment. They went through my medical history, reviewed my medications, took my blood pressure and pulse, gave me a pregnancy test, and took eight vials of blood. They monitor its effects by blood samples throughout the trial.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7e292c282c500018c793a7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hardy&#39;s Instagram story the day she got her vaccine\" height=\"1792\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Hardy&#39;s Instagram story the day she got the first shot.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Elle Hardy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>I was told that the study is double blind, meaning the doctors don't know if you get the vaccine or a placebo, and neither do you. I had a 50/50 chance of getting the vaccine.&#160;<p>All told, the first vaccine process took three hours, and they paid me $150 for my time. Each day for the first week after the shot I had to fill out a check-up form on an app, measuring temperature and rating different symptoms, before receiving a phone call from the doctor at the end of each week to see if I was okay. If you do fall sick, they said they take care of you at their medical facility, but I haven't needed that.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7e2c0cc655f6001969ece4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The app Elle Hardy uses to check in during the vaccine trial\" height=\"1711\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The app Hardy uses to check in during the vaccine trial.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Elle Hardy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>The side effects were a little unpleasant, but nowhere near as bad as they could be getting COVID-19.</h2><p>I didn't feel 100% for a few days after the first shot. It felt like that day or two when you're on the cusp of getting the flu, but it didn't interfere with my work or life. My upper left arm where the shot was put into was swollen and incredibly sore for days. I couldn't lie on it or even pick up a cup of coffee with that hand. I had a similar reaction to the MMR vaccine in high school, so I began to think that I'd definitely received the mRNA shot and not the placebo.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7cb97c282c500018c78eed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"medical coronavirus flu virus covid19 hospital doctor nurse tools stethoscope blood pressure pills vitamins medicine pharmacy pharmaceutical lab vaccine cox 25\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>&#34;I had a similar reaction to the MMR vaccine in high school, so I began to think that I&#39;d definitely received the mRNA shot and not the placebo.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Crystal Cox/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>After about four days, all of the symptoms disappeared. The booster shot 28 days later had similar effects, but they went away more quickly, within about 48 hours.</p><p>My curiosity got the better of me, and I decided to get an antibody test to see if my suspicions were correct. I'd had one earlier in the summer and it came back negative. This time, it came back positive. Of course, I can't be certain that it was from the vaccine, but I haven't had any COVID-19 symptoms and neither has anyone in my social bubble.</p><h2>It's good news, but I'm not changing the way I act.</h2><p>I was thrilled to know that I have antibodies, but I'm still taking all of the usual precautions, especially around wearing a mask and avoiding unventilated spaces. It's just a basic decency to be considerate to others around you.&#160;</p><p>Furthermore, the presence of antibodies doesn't mean that you're bulletproof ‚Äî the whole point of the vaccine trial is to figure out whether the shot works to prevent the coronavirus. Plus, antibodies may recede over time or not be an absolute barrier to infection. Still, it's given me hope that there's an end in sight for all of us.</p><p>My concern is that some media outlets will sensationalize any problems with the vaccine, such as what we saw in England recently when a subject in the Oxford vaccine trial became ill and the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/sep/12/oxford-university-resumes-covid-19-vaccine-trials\">trial was briefly paused</a>. People should be informed, but I suspect that any stories to do with vaccine timing will get a lot of clicks, and we live in a time where misinformation spreads as fast as coronavirus.</p><h2>I hope that my experience gives people hope that we can get through this.</h2><p>There's research that indicates that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/poll-third-of-americans-wont-take-a-coronavirus-vaccine-2020-9\">one third of Americans</a> don't want to take the vaccine. I've had friends who aren't anti-vaxxers tell me this ‚Äî they're concerned that a cure is being rushed out to help with the election or get people back to work.</p><p>What worries me more than any side effects of the vaccine is that, given how much more we know about the virus and the ways it spreads now, we still aren't being particularly targeted and effective when it comes to testing and tracing.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e94c9f9c023200c2f766295?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Moderna CEO Stephane Bancel\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Moderna CEO Stephane Bancel attends a meeting with President Donald Trump, members of the Coronavirus Task Force, and pharmaceutical executives in the Cabinet Room of the White House on March 2, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Harnik/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Nor have the best ways to stay safe been well communicated. It took us months to learn that masks and <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2020/07/why-arent-we-talking-more-about-airborne-transmission/614737/\">ventilated spaces are critical</a> to stopping the spread. We also don't seem to be doing much about <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2020/09/k-overlooked-variable-driving-pandemic/616548/\">super-spreader events and cluster busting</a>. Many Asian countries are <a href=\"https://www.stuff.co.nz/national/health/coronavirus/122443097/coronavirus-rapid-cluster-busting-to-find-covid19-outbreak-source-could-nip-other-clusters-in-the-bud\">really good at this</a>, and consequently have managed the pandemic far better than the United States.</p><p>As one of few people who's experienced the pandemic response in several countries, I have no doubt that the US has handled it worse than most, and that it's cost lives. We can only hope that governments and agencies can come together to administer the vaccine quickly and give people the confidence to get the shot when it comes ‚Äî which may be widely available <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/10/01/health/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-bancel-bn/index.html\">as soon as March 2021</a>, according to the Moderna CEO.</p><p><em>This article was originally published on Business Insider October 13, 2020. It has been updated with new information.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 1/cdn27@2020_3/2020/11/16/16-46-25-157_b6a721cc38407993.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138283},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Walmart is selling the bulk of its stake in Seiyu, the Japanese supermarket chain. The deal values Seiyu at $1.6 billion.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-seiyu-deal-kkr-rakuten-walmart-japan-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb27cbf402d49001924f120?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Seiyu\" height=\"2202\" width=\"2937\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kyodo News Stills/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Walmart is selling a majority stake in its Japanese supermarket chain Seiyu, <a href=\"https://corporate.walmart.com/newsroom/2020/11/15/kkr-and-rakuten-to-acquire-stakes-in-seiyu-from-walmart-focus-on-accelerating-digital-transformation-of-japanese-retail\">it announced Sunday</a>.</li>\n<li>The deal values Seiyu at 172.5 billion yen ($1.6 billion), far lower than Walmart reportedly sought in 2018.</li>\n<li>Walmart is selling a 65% stake to KKR and a minority stake to Rakuten, retaining 15% stake.</li>\n<li>Seiyu has 331 stores across Japan, but the three investors want to focus on expanding its e-commerce.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Walmart is selling a majority stake in 300-store Japanese supermarket chain Seiyu, <a href=\"https://corporate.walmart.com/newsroom/2020/11/15/kkr-and-rakuten-to-acquire-stakes-in-seiyu-from-walmart-focus-on-accelerating-digital-transformation-of-japanese-retail\">it announced Sunday</a>.</p><p>The deal valued Seiyu at 172.5 billion yen ($1.6 billion) including debt.</p><p>This valuation is far less than what Walmart reportedly sought in 2018, when <a href=\"https://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2018/07/12/business/corporate-business/16-year-struggle-seiyu-walmart-looks-next-retailer-exit-japan/\">Japanese media reported</a> it wanted to sell Seiyu.</p><p>The deal also takes Walmart a step closer to exiting the country: Seiyu is the biggest part of Walmart Japan's business.</p><p>The retailer is selling a 65% stake to global investment firm KKR and 20% stake to Japanese e-commerce company Rakuten, which has already worked with Seiyu for its grocery delivery service.</p><p>Walmart will retain a 15% stake.&#160;</p><p>Walmart first invested in Seiyu in 2002 when it bought a 6% stake, marking its first venture into the Japanese retail market. Walmart gradually increased its stake, before taking over the chain in 2008.</p><p>Walmart will now work alongside KKR and Rakuten to accelerate Seiyu's digital growth, Walmart said.&#160;This includes introducing more options for cashless payment and investing in shopping apps.</p><p>During the transition period, Seiyu CEO Lionel Desclee will continue to lead the business, before taking on a new role within Walmart.</p><p>Representatives from KKR, Rakuten, and Walmart will form a new board of directors, which will appoint a new CEO for once the transaction is closed. This is expected to happen in the first quarter of 2021.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-wants-to-rival-amazon-advertising-but-pushes-out-agencies-2020-10?r=gd-sub\">Walmart is building a big ad business to rival Amazon, but it's causing friction with some agencies that control a big chunk of the $17 billion market</a></em></p><p>In 2018, <a href=\"https://www.japantimes.co.jp/news/2018/07/12/business/corporate-business/16-year-struggle-seiyu-walmart-looks-next-retailer-exit-japan/\">Japanese media reported</a> Walmart was looking to sell Seiyu for around 300 billion to 500 billion yen ($2.86 billion to $4.77 billion), which potential buyers reportedly deemed too expensive.</p><p>In October, Walmart <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-sells-asda-for-8-8-billion-2020-10\">sold </a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-sells-asda-for-8-8-billion-2020-10\">UK grocery chain Asda for $8.8 billion</a> after 21 years of ownership, marking a near-exit from the UK.</p><p>But Walmart is scaling up its operations in other countries such as India, where the e-commerce market in booming. In July, Walmart <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-e-commerce-305-million-indian-investment-invests-injection-2020-7\">injected $1.2 billion‚Å† into Indian e-commerce giant Flipkart</a>, two years after it bought a 77% stake for $16 billion.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-seiyu-deal-kkr-rakuten-walmart-japan-2020-11'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a year.</p>\n<p>But Thanksgiving celebrations tend to be hourslong affairs, and the free version of Zoom that most people are using has a hard limit of 40 minutes per meeting.&nbsp;</p>\n<p>In a very 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Special operations snipers are about to get this 'awesome' new rifle of choice for US military sharpshooters","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/special-operations-snipers-are-getting-this-awesome-new-sniper-rifle-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2990d402d49001924f182?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A US Army Special Operation Soldier with 3rd Battalion, 7th Special Forces Group (Airborne) fires a legacy M2010 Enhanced Sniper Rifle\" height=\"414\" width=\"828\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A US Army soldier with 3rd Battalion, 7th Special Forces Group (Airborne) fires a legacy M2010 Enhanced Sniper Rifle.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Marine Corps photo by Lance Cpl. William Chockey</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>US Special Operations Command has ordered its first Multi-Role Adaptive Design (MRAD) Mk 22 sniper rifles, which are expected to be delivered in January 2021.</li>\n<li>The Army and the Marines have also said they want to acquire the modular, multi-caliber weapon.</li>\n<li>\"It's an awesome gun,\" a seasoned Army sniper told Insider earlier this year, adding that he never saw anything he didn't like on the gun.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>US special-operations snipers will soon be receiving the new sniper rifle that everyone in the military wants to get their hands on.</p><p>Barrett Firearms Manufacturing has received an initial production order for the new Mk 22 Multi-Role Adaptive Design (MRAD) sniper rifle from US Special Operations Command, <a href=\"https://news.barrett.net/2020/11/13/barrett-receives-first-mk22-delivery-order-from-ussocom/\">the company announced</a> Friday, as <a href=\"https://taskandpurpose.com/military-tech/us-military-sniper-rifle-barrett-mrad-special-operations-command\">Task &#38; Purpose first reported</a>.</p><p>Barrett reports that its rifle has met the requirements of the Department of Defense and has completed production qualification testing and operational testing.</p><p>\"We are pleased to have reached this milestone with the project and look forward to providing our warfighters with this highly capable platform,\" Joel Miller, Barrett's director of global military sales, said in a statement.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e554630fee23d02975621c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Barrett Firearms Multi-Role Adaptive Design (MRAD) bolt-action sniper rifle\" height=\"2992\" width=\"5984\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Barrett Firearms Multi-Role Adaptive Design (MRAD) bolt-action sniper rifle.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy photo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>SOCOM first started looking for a new modular, multi-caliber sniper rifle in 2016, and in March 2019, the command awarded Barrett a $49.9 million contract for the MRAD rifle under its Advanced Sniper Rifle (ASR) program. Fielding is expected to start in January 2021.</p><p>What makes the MRAD different from other rifles is that it can be chambered in 7.62 x 51 mm NATO, .300 Norma Magnum, and .338 Norma Magnum ammunition, each of which has a different purpose on the battlefield.</p><p>\"It gives more flexibility to the sniper as to what configuration to put it in and what targets they are going after,\" US Army Lt. Col. Chris Kennedy, chief of lethality in the soldier requirements division of the Maneuver Center of Excellence, previously told Insider.</p><p>Both the Army and the Marines also want the Mk 22 MRAD rifle for their snipers.</p><p>In their respective Fiscal Year 2021 budget requests, the Army asked for 536 MRAD sniper rifles for a little over $10 million under its Precision Sniper Rifle (PSR) program to replace the M2010 and M107 rifles, and the Marines asked for 250 rifles for $4 million under SOCOM's ASR program.</p><p>The Marines expect the new rifle to \"replace all current bolt-action sniper rifles in the Marine Corps,\" according to the latest budget request.</p><p>In the budget documents, the Marines wrote that the new rifles offer \"extended range, greater lethality, and a wider variety of special purpose ammunition.\" The Army argued that the weapon \"increases stand-off distances ensuring overmatch against enemy counter sniper engagements and increases sniper capability.\"</p><p>The new sniper rifle, which is also lighter than some legacy systems, \"will become the primary anti-personnel Sniper Weapon System (SWS) in all Army Sniper Teams,\" the Army added.</p><p>\"It's an awesome gun,\" 1st Sgt. Kevin Sipes, a seasoned Army sniper, told Insider earlier this year.</p><p>\"I can tell you I never saw anything on that gun that I didn't like,\" he said. \"It shoots phenomenally well. What it does, as far as barrel changes and things like that go, is pretty exceptional.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a multiple reports.</p><p>Trump is considering a number of moves against The Communist Party of China, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-11-15/trump-plans-last-minute-china-crackdown-to-trip-up-biden-axios?utm_campaign=socialflow-organic&utm_content=business&cmpid=socialflow-facebook-business&utm_medium=social&utm_source=facebook_source=facebook\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg reported</a>, including further sanctions against party officials and institutions involved in China's oppression of Hong Kong and Xinjiang, combating illegal fishing, and shielding US tech companies from Chinese exploitation.</p><p>The moves, expected in the next few weeks, are designed at least partly to leave President-elect Joe Biden with little room to manoeuvre in regards to Washington's relationship with Beijing, according to Bloomberg.</p><p><a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/11/15/politics/trump-administration-china-biden/index.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">CNN reported</a> that the Trump administration believes it will box in the incoming Biden administration when it comes to dealing with Beijing, citing government officials.</p><p>The US-China relationship has deteriorated over the course of Trump's presidency over issues including trade, China's actions in Hong Kong, and the outbreak of the coronavirus which Trump has blamed on Beijing and dubbed \"the China virus.\"</p><p><a href=\"https://www.axios.com/cuellar-progressive-policy-south-texas-trump-biden-c3c1bab4-cbbf-422f-b4b9-524d98889a8b.html?utm_campaign=organic&utm_medium=socialshare&utm_source=twitter=twitter\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">An Axios report suggests</a> that the Trump administration is also considering expanding a Defense Department list of Chinese companies that are blocked from US investment due to their links to the Chinese military. Officials are also looking at taking further action against Beijing's use of forced labour in the fishing industry, the report said.</p><p>John Ullyot, National Security Council spokesperson, told both publications: \"Unless Beijing reverses course and becomes a responsible player on the global stage, future US presidents will find it politically suicidal to reverse President Trump's historic actions.\"</p><p>Trump's team could fill senior government positions with people who have more hawkish views on Beijing, according to Axios. href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/5VpfJdVEv2I\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 16 Nov 2020 12:40:08 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb2719f402d49001924f10e?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"6cfacd90a62f3d40957e1796fc0ee0c4","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn74@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-20-119_7aa3da9e5facea5e.webp","destWidth":1976,"destHeight":1482,"sourceBytes":207234,"destBytes":207234,"author":"apayne@businessinsider.com (Adam Payne)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb24475402d49001924f0c1?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn48@2020_2/2020/11/16/16-46-25-244_476fab06aeca347e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn92@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-890_a5be29a5e9e52243.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn63@2020_3/2020/11/16/16-46-22-417_373ef69b97157207.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5VpfJdVEv2I:RUKue-bsxRw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn47@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-26-024_364d6f9da65726fe.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/5VpfJdVEv2I":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn59@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-25-279_f8fc7f569bfedcad.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138317},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"8 time management mistakes that are making you less productive","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/time-management-mistakes-making-you-less-productive-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f9897636f5b310011723c0a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Woman working at home desktop computer\" height=\"1405\" width=\"2133\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Give up the idea that the busier you are, the more competent you seem ‚Äî it&#39;s not helping your productivity.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cecilie_Arcurs/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If you feel like you need more hours in the day to get work done, you might be putting unnecessary pressure on yourself.</li>\n<li>Learn to find \"autonomous control\" over your time by budgeting your hours more wisely, enforcing boundaries, and focusing on one task at a time.</li>\n<li>Let go of the \"have it all mentality,\" and gradually find a cadence in your work speed that helps you stay concentrated and efficient.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A couple of weekends ago, I was asked to join a Zoom meeting. My immediate response, \"I don't have time for that.\" The thing is, I could have squeezed the event into my schedule. I had to remind myself that, \"No, I'm not crunched for time.\"</p><p>Like most people, I only perceived that I had a limited supply of time. In reality, we all have the availability to cross items off our to-do list or enjoy our leisure time. However, you probably feel like you don't because you're putting unnecessary pressure on yourself.</p><p>In short, you aren't really crunched for time. You've just tricked yourself into thinking that because of&#160;the following eight reasons.</p><h2>1. You haven't created and stuck to your time budget</h2><p>Your time, just like your finances, is a valuable resource that needs to be managed. If you don't create and stick to your budget, then you won't have enough time for what's important to you. Even worse, you may end up putting yourself in debt.</p><p>For instance, if you work 60 hours per week, that means you won't have as much downtime. That means you're going to sacrifice quality time with your nearest and dearest. You may even be putting your health and well-being in jeopardy.</p><p>In short,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.calendar.com/blog/how-to-create-a-time-budget-and-stick-to-it/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener nofollow sponsored\">a time budget</a>&#160;as defined by Amanda Abella in a Calendar article is \"a guideline that helps you spend your time the way you want to spend it.\" Obviously, this also includes the things that you aren't crazy about doing. But, the concept is that having a time budget will make it manage your time wisely and with more intention.</p><p>To get started, determine what matters to you in life. Often, this would be your relationships, health, and career. Knowing this, you would spend your workweek only on activities that push you closer to your goals. And during your downtime, you would work out or spend time with your family.</p><p>How can you stick to your budget? A calendar app and boundaries are important because if you have an activity scheduled, it makes it easier to enforce boundaries.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/8-ways-to-make-yourself-job-indispensable-post-covid-19-2020-5\">8 ways to make yourself indispensable at work during COVID-19, according to an executive coach</a></em></p><h2>2. You're looking for control</h2><p>\"When we say that someone 'has more time' than someone else, we do not mean that she has literally a twenty-fifth hour in her day,\"&#160;<a href=\"https://press.uchicago.edu/books/excerpt/2015/Wajcman_Pressed_for_Time.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">noted</a> Robert E. Goodin in \"Discretionary Time: A New Measure of Freedom.\" \"Rather, we mean to say that she has fewer constraints and more choices in how she can choose to spend her time. She has more 'autonomous control' over her time,\" he explained.&#160;</p><p>Why's this the case? Psychologist and behavioral scientist Susan Weinschenk believes it's because <a href=\"https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/brain-wise/201301/why-having-choices-makes-us-feel-powerful\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">\"we equate having choices with having control.\"</a></p><p>\"Our survival instincts tell us that we'll survive if we have control,\" clarified Weinschenk. \"So it's our powerful unconscious that keeps us seeking control, and it's the desire for control that keeps us seeking choices.\"</p><h2>3. You believe in the myth of multitasking</h2><p><a href=\"https://www.calendar.com/blog/the-myth-of-multitasking/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">When I talk about multitasking</a>, I'm not referring to mindless or mundane tasks that are taking place in the background. For example, you can fold your laundry or wash dishes while listening to a podcast. Another example would be going for a walk while talking on the phone.</p><p>Instead, the type of multitasking I'm referring to here tasks that require your complete attention. Case in point, it's not effective to work on your taxes while simultaneously writing tomorrow's meeting agenda. The reason for this is because the brain is set up to handle only one thing at a time.</p><p>It's also been found that multitasking can slow you down, and&#160;because you're more likely to make mistakes, multitasking can take you longer to complete tasks.</p><p>The solution? It's pretty simple, actually. Do one thing at a time, aka single-tasking.</p><h2>4. Fueling conflicts, not passion</h2><p>Research shows that those who are passionate and doing activities that matter aren't as rushed and harried. The reason? It prevents inner conflicts.</p><p>\"Employees lacking in passion said that their goals were competing with each other, fighting for time and attention,\" explained Kira M. Newman, managing editor of <a href=\"https://greatergood.berkeley.edu/article/item/why_you_never_seem_to_have_enough_time\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Greater Good</a>. However, passionate employees were different, viewing their goals as supporting each other.&#160;</p><p>\"Time pressure isn't just about how enjoyable our activities are, but also how well they fit together in our heads,\" added Newman.&#160;</p><p>How can you resolve this in your own life? Well, there's no right or wrong way. But, you should definitely let go of the \"have it all mentality.\" Instead, schedule your priorities and activities that you enjoy and find fulfilling.</p><p>If you still feel overwhelmed,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.gsb.stanford.edu/insights/jennifer-aaker-why-we-pay-save-time\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Stanford GSB professor Jennifer Aaker&#160;</a>and her team found that there are two simple interventions that can help. The first is \"to breathe so that each complete breath (inhale plus exhale) lasts 11 counts.\" The second was reappraising anxiety as excitement, like saying \"I am excited!\"</p><h2>5. You aren't heading for the hills</h2><p>Have you ever run a marathon? If so, you definitely had to do some training, and you may have used something called the Fartlek approach.</p><p>It's a Swedish term that means \"speed play.\" It's a type of interval training where you alternate between fast segments and slow jogs in order to improve your speed and endurance. But, it's also recommended that you&#160;<a href=\"https://www.runnersworld.com/advanced/a20823905/maximize-your-training-time/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">add hills to your run</a>.</p><p>What does this have to do with&#160;<a href=\"https://www.entrepreneur.com/topic/time-management\" data-ga-category=\"autotag-linking\" data-ga-label=\"ent-tags\" data-ga-action=\"/topic/time-management\">time management</a>? Well, just like increasing your speed and strength, you also need to challenge yourself. For example,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.calendar.com/blog/learn-how-to-concentrate-your-focus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">learning how to concentrate your focus</a>&#160;of block out distractions. Both require discipline, practice, and a balance between sprints and breaks.</p><p>Of course, don't just attack these hills. Gradually work your way up. After all, you don't want to burn yourself out before entering the race, right?</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tips-help-small-business-owners-entrepreneurs-have-good-mental-health\">7 ways entrepreneurs and business owners can better manage their mental health and wellbeing</a></em></p><h2>6. Ask if you'd do it tomorrow</h2><p>Have you read Laura Vanderkam's time management book \"Juliet's School of Possibilities\"? If not, you should. It's a solid read full of excellent advice. But, this is probably my favorite nugget of wisdom: The lead character informs a young consultant, Riley, that she only says \"yes\" to what she wants to do. \"Most people, however, have a very vague sense of opportunity cost,\" <a href=\"https://www.fastcompany.com/90317324/how-to-feel-like-you-have-enough-time\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">wrote</a>&#160;Vanderkam. \"When someone asks you to do something far in the future, you might look at your calendar and see that it seems pretty open.\"</p><p>But, she adds, this is actually a fallacy. The reason? Your future self is going to be just as busy as you currently are. \"You'll feel just as swamped, only now you'll also have this other commitment competing for your time and energy (that you didn't want to do in the first place).\"</p><p>He suggests that you should ask yourself whether you'd be willing to do something tomorrow, knowing how busy you are now. If the answer is yes, then say yes.&#160;And&#160;if the answer is no, well, \"that's the best response for the future too. When you're more judicious with your 'yes,' you can free up all kinds of space.\"</p><h2>7. You're focused too much on the money</h2><p>You obviously need money to survive. And&#160;you kind of need it to engage in hobbies. At the same time,&#160;<a href=\"https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=1694704\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">research</a>&#160;from Sanford DeVoe of the University of Toronto and Jeffrey Pfeffer of Stanford found that those with higher-incomes feel more time-crunched.</p><p>As explained in&#160;<a href=\"https://www.economist.com/christmas-specials/2014/12/20/why-is-everyone-so-busy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">The Economist</a>; \"Once hours are financially quantified, people worry more about wasting, saving, or using them profitably. When economies grow and incomes rise, everyone's time becomes more valuable. And the more valuable something becomes, the scarcer it seems.\"</p><p>Moreover, DeVoe and Pfeffer found that just the perception of affluence can make you feel like you don't have enough time. So, while you should certainly make a comfortable living, you also don't need to be obsessed about it.</p><h2>8. Being busy is a status symbol</h2><p>Via&#160;<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Overwhelmed-Work-Love-Play-When/dp/0374228442\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">Overwhelmed: Work, Love, and Play When No One Has the Time</a>: \"Psychologists write of treating burned-out clients who can't shake the notion that the busier you are, the more you are thought of as competent, smart, successful, admired, and even envied.\"</p><p>The fix here is to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.calendar.com/blog/stop-worrying-about-being-productive/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">stop worrying about being productive</a>&#160;24/7. For some, that may be a strange concept. But, the fact is that you don't need to maximize every moment of your day.</p><p>Instead, spend your valuable time on the people and projects that matter. Additionally, avoid falling into the busyness trap and just enjoy yourself. Remember, life is too short to work around the clock. Sometimes you just need to slow down and have a little fun.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Election week, Trump, and the chaos of 2020 prove that cable news feels more outdated than ever","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/cable-news-coverage-election-week-analysis-outdated-format-2020-11","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b509f4019032f1d008b47b1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Analysis banner\" height=\"61\" width=\"1201\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeb844402d49001924ed0d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"cable news coverage election week 2020\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cable news coverage during election week stressed people out, but it didn&#39;t have to be this way.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Spencer Platt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The stress of election week didn't have to be as bad as it was.</li>\n<li>Despite warnings from network hosts, the hour-by-hour model of cable news and its attention grabbing alerts were poorly suited for the procedural quirks of the 2020 election.</li>\n<li>While the 2000 election dragged on for longer and its margin was much closer, the relentless attention economy of 2020 made this election seem similarly agonizing.</li>\n<li>Unlike the music industry, cable has not structurally shifted nearly as much in the digital and streaming era.</li>\n<li>With President Donald Trump refusing to concede the election, these issues are that only becoming more pronounced.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Watching the election returns last week thoroughly stressed out a huge number of Americans.</p><p>Things haven't been much better this week, with President Donald Trump refusing to concede the election and waging factually meritless legal challenges along with a disinformation campaign that could further undermine faith in the democratic process.</p><p>Stories like \"<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/10/31/at-home/election-stress.html\">how to avoid election stress</a>\" or \"<a href=\"https://www.healthline.com/health/cope-with-stress-before-and-after-election\">7 tips to cope with stress before and after the election</a>\" have become widespread. Many news outlets, including Insider, made efforts to prepare the public for the likelihood of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/america-likely-wont-know-presidential-race-winner-on-election-night-2020-5\">not knowing a winner on election night.</a> Yet for many Americans, the hypothetical proposition of an election week instead of election night hit much harder once we were stuck living in it.</p><p>The very format of cable news tracking incremental vote returns 24/7 made the increasing stress an inevitable outcome for those tuning in.</p><p>After closely monitoring Fox News, CNN and MSNBC throughout last week and into this week's chaos, differences in coverage choices between the three networks have largely been overridden by one common trait.</p><p>The need to fill every hour with new content ‚Äî or, rather, simulating the feeling of newness even if few developments are actually taking place ‚Äî is at the crux of cable news' problem coming out of the 2020 election.</p><p>If watching election week on TV taught us anything new, it's that cable news feels more outdated than ever before.</p><h3>This restless nightmare was 20 years in the making</h3><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faed6fb1c741f0019ac9b91?format=jpeg\" alt=\"florida 2000 vote count hanging chad\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Observers inspect and count ballots during the hand recount of presidential ballots at the Palm Beach County Emergency Operations Center on November 19, 2000 West Palm Beach, Florida.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Robert King/Newsmakers via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The 2000 election's five-week limbo period, culminating in the Supreme Court's Bush v. Gore decision, was clearly a much more strung out event.</p><p>However, cable news was still in its relative infancy back then and smartphones didn't exist yet, or social media.</p><p>Our attention economy in 2020 is almost incomparable to that of 2000.</p><p>During those 20 years, cable news became more sophisticated but its business model largely remained the same.</p><p>As the 24-hour news cycle became part of American life, the competition for ratings and ad revenue through hourly programming remained in tact even as the digital landscape evolved dramatically.</p><p>While music lables have substantially pivoted in their business models over the course of these two decades, Cable has yet to undergo such a shift even as networks have launched their own streaming services. Offerings like FOX Nation and NBC News NOW have a broad array of talent at their disposal, but they remain firmly in second fiddle territory when it comes to where lawmakers and political figures go for interviews, and what they prioritize strategically.</p><h3>Big boards and lead changes did not work the same way in 2020</h3><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faee0991c741f0019ac9bce?format=jpeg\" alt=\"snl cnn big board skit\" height=\"1029\" width=\"2059\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Beck Bennett as Wolf Blitzer and Alex Moffat as John King during the &#34;Biden Victory&#34; Cold Open on Saturday, November 7, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Will Heath/NBC/NBCU Photo Bank via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The main cable networks did not cover election week in a monolithic way from an editorial judgment standpoint, and anchors across Fox News, CNN and MSNBC repeatedly warned their viewers they might be in for the long haul.</p><p>But all three featured the same mainstays from their election coverage in recent cycles, particularly chyrons with the vote totals and a percentage of precincts reporting as well as the so-called big board, an interactive touch screen display with results and maps on it.</p><p>Two skippers at the helm of their respective big boards ‚Äî John King of CNN and Steve Kornacki of MSNBC and NBC News ‚Äî became borderline folk heroes and certified memes throughout the week.</p><p>Both Kornacki and King provided clarity and caution in their performances at the board, earning widespread praise to accompany being immortalized in internet humor.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Cat Mama  (@_chloepaige) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1324585547919220736?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 6, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1324801259698855936?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 6, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Late Night with Seth Meyers  (@LateNightSeth) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1324465800846155776?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 5, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>But what made big boards and vote tickers helpful in past elections only added to the stress and anxiety of this one.</p><p>Right away on election night, CNN's Wolf Blitzer kept cutting off King to point out incremental changes in leads, despite the fact that the vast majority of precincts had yet to report their results. His interruptions were essentially meaningless with such a long night and week ahead.</p><p>The specific ordering of how the mail-in votes arrived through the night and week led to the <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/explainer-red-mirage-blue-mirage-beware-of-early-us-election-wins-2020-11\">predicted and well documented problem</a> of the \"red mirage,\" which showed Trump to be ahead only for more populated counties to push Biden over the top with their mail-in votes later on.</p><p>Despite these networks having deep benches of reporters and correspondents with specific areas of expertise, lots of time was dedicate to panels of political strategists and other pundits who were not as well versed in the procedural peculiarities of this election.</p><p>Fox News in particular struggled with Trump surrogates spreading false claims about voter fraud, an issue that lingered this week on the network even as hosts like Bret Baier and Sandra Smith remained diligent in reminding viewers when the claims had no evidence behind them.</p><p>Versions of this short-term framing coupled with the threat of disinformation continued through the week, culminating in the major networks waiting until Saturday morning to call the race for Biden.</p><p><em>Read more</em>: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-ddhq-and-business-insider-called-the-election-for-biden-2020-11\">Why Decision Desk HQ and Insider called the election for Joe Biden</a></p><p>Now that we're in a different kind of limbo as Trump refuses to concede <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/world-moved-on-from-trump-even-if-gop-allies-havent-2020-11\">despite world leaders already moving on and congratulating Biden as the winner</a>, Americans are once again tuning in and experiencing the same kinds of anxiety-provoking issues.</p><p>The likes of Kornacki and King aren't the problem here, nor are the tweaks networks made to how they planned on the likelihood of a drawn out process.</p><p>The fundamental flaw is the 24/7 news cycle itself, from the flashy chyrons to the breaking news and \"key race alert\" alert jingles ‚Äî <a href=\"https://www.morningbrew.com/marketing/stories/2020/11/06/headspace-calm-key-race-alert-partnership-wasnt-oneoff\">ironically sponsored by Calm on CNN</a>.</p><p>With all of the networks looking at how to <a href=\"https://qz.com/1928175/cable-news-dominated-election-night-tv-ratings/\">stay viable beyond their ageing audiences</a>, all of the incentives are in place for a structural shift.</p><p>But it hasn't happened yet, and until it does, tuning in for election coverage will have to come at the price of overeager anchors and panelists, abrasive musical cues, and bright maps of red and blue being seared into our psyches.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Gaming giant Capcom says the data of up to 350,000 people, including players, was stolen in a massive ransomware attack","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/capcom-hack-ransomware-attack-hackers-customer-data-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb26ce3402d49001924f10a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Resident Evil 2\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Gamers play Capcom&#39;s &#39;Resident Evil 2 Remake&#39; during Paris Games Week on October 27, 2018 in Paris, France.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chesnot/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Gaming giant Capcom said Monday it was hit with a hack that may have compromised the personal data of up to 350,000 individuals, including players.</li>\n<li>The hack was a ransomware attack that scrambled Capcom's servers on November 2.</li>\n<li>The data compromised included names, email addresses, and phone numbers, but not credit card information.</li>\n<li>\"Capcom offers its sincerest apologies for any complications and concerns that this may bring to its potentially impacted customers as well as to its many stakeholders,\" the company said in a statement.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Japanese gaming giant Capcom has confirmed it's been hit with a major cyberattack in which hackers stole the data of up to 350,000 people.</p><p>The company, known for hit franchises including \"Street Fighter,\" \"Resident Evil,\" and \"Monster Hunter,\" said in a <a href=\"http://www.capcom.co.jp/ir/english/news/html/e201116.html\">statement</a> Monday that it first detected a problem on the morning of November 2.</p><p>\"Capcom confirmed that this was a targeted attack against the company using ransomware, which destroyed and encrypted data on its servers,\" the company said.</p><p>Capcom first broke the news of the suspected attack on November 4, and on November 12 it publicly announced that some corporate information and data belonging to nine present and former employees had been stolen.</p><p>Its Monday announcement confirmed, however, that the scope of the attack was far broader, and may have included players' personal data.</p><p>The company estimated a maximum of 350,000 individuals' personal data may have been stolen. This included the data from players, shareholders, plus former employees and their family members.</p><p>The data included names, email addresses, and phone numbers, but not credit card information.</p><p>Capcom said it will contact anyone who it can confirm has definitely had their data compromised.</p><p>In ransomware attacks, hackers lock a target out of their own data and then essentially hold it hostage, threatening to either leak or destroy the data unless the target pays a ransom.</p><p>Capcom said it was contacted by a hacking group calling itself Rag nar Locker demanding payment, at which point it contacted the police force in Osaka, Japan.</p><p>The company did not explicitly state in its press release whether it paid the ransom or not. A representative was not immediately available to comment.</p><p>\"Capcom offers its sincerest apologies for any complications and concerns that this may bring to its potentially impacted customers as well as to its many stakeholders,\" the company said in a statement. It added that its investigation was still ongoing.</p><p>Capcom said it has contacted both Japan and the UK's data protection watchdogs. It has engaged a security company and a software consultancy to inspect its systems, the company said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Isobel Asher Hamilton)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb26ce3402d49001924f10a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn48@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-45-52-698_7407a46da5f54a36.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=TP01lRM8y1s:dQfWQmQKBuE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn64@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-21-318_b784156a70090082.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=TP01lRM8y1s:dQfWQmQKBuE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn83@2020_5/2020/11/16/16-46-23-210_7a6c98f3b0914c3a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=TP01lRM8y1s:dQfWQmQKBuE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn99@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-22-024_2e3c6dc2aa15d8f3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/TP01lRM8y1s":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn35@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-46-21-302_26fe66a305a60d46.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138321},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"What would happen if you jumped off the International Space Station","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-if-jump-off-international-space-station-2018-6","description":"<div style=\"position:relative; overflow:hidden; padding-bottom:56.25%\">\n<iframe src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/Hz2lozP6-jZbcmOYf.html\"\nwidth=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"auto\" title=\"What would happen if you jumped off the International Space Station\"\nstyle=\"position:absolute;\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>SpaceX's Crew Dragon spaceship&#160;launch to the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-pictures-astronauts-international-space-station-2016-12\">International Space Station</a> is the start of a<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-launches-rocket-mission-nasa-astronauts-crew-1-dragon-spaceship-2020-11\">&#160;six-month mission, where astronauts will live and work on the orbiting laboratory.</a></li>\n<li>While the sight from the International Space Station is a beautiful one, jumping off of it wouldn't be.</li>\n<li>If an astronaut tried to reach Earth's surface by jumping, it would be a deadly journey filled with hypersonic speeds and intense heat.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><em>Following is the transcript of the video.</em></p><p><strong>Narrator: </strong>Most skydivers jump off a plane flying 3.8 km above the ground. But imagine jumping off something even higher, like the International Space Station.</p><p>Unless you have a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-iron-man-suit-missing-and-its-worth-320000-2018-5\">supersuit</a> like Tony Stark, it's not gonna end well. But let's pretend Iron Man lends you one.</p><p>Ok, ready? 3 ‚Ä¶ 2 ‚Ä¶ 1 ‚Ä¶ Jump! Wait ‚Ä¶ what?</p><p>That's right, you wouldn't fall straight down. In fact, it'll take you at least 2.5 years before you reach the surface. So what's going on?</p><p>Height isn't the main reason your fall takes so long. In fact, if you fell like a normal <a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/luke-aikins-skydived-without-a-parachute-net-california-2016-8\">skydiver</a>, it would only take about 2 hours.</p><p>But the thing is, you don't fall straight down. You fall into orbit. The reason is speed. You see, the <a href=\"http://www.businessinsider.com/solar-eclipse-space-station-nasa-photos-video-2017-8\">ISS</a> might be called a station, but it's hardly stationary.&#160; It's actually moving 12 times faster than a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fighter-jets-us-air-force-2018-4\">jet fighter</a>.</p><p>If you shot anything at that speed on Earth, by the time it was about to hit the ground, it would miss! In the same way, the ISS isn't floating in space, it's falling towards Earth and missing!</p><p>And when you jump off the ISS, you're initially moving at that same speed. So you end up in orbit, too ‚Äî at least for a while.</p><p>Now, even though it's so high up, the ISS is pushing through a very thin atmosphere. And that friction slows it down. So the station fires engines to maintain speed and keep from crashing into the Earth.</p><p>But sadly your supersuit doesn't come with engines strapped to your feet. This has two consequences:</p><p>First, it means you can't maneuver and have to hope that any of those 13,000 chunks of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/space-debris-around-earth-2016-1\">space debris</a> don't impale you. Second, without rockets to maintain your speed, you'll slow down and spiral toward Earth.</p><p>But it won't be quick. The Chinese space station <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chinese-space-station-crash-tiangong-1-south-pacific-2018-4\">Tiangong 1</a>, for example, about 2 years to fall out of orbit. On the ISS, you're higher up, so you'll take roughly 2.5 years. But once you strike the atmosphere, your long wait is over. And it's go time.</p><p>As you re-enter, you have one goal: slow down. You're traveling at hypersonic speeds. So, if you deployed a parachute now, it'll shred to pieces.</p><p>And that's not the only problem. Falling through the atmosphere at such break-neck speeds generates a lot of pressure on your suit ‚Äî at least 8Gs of force ‚Äî that's 8 times the gravity you feel at sea level.</p><p>And if you're falling feet first, that'll push the blood away from your brain and toward your feet. So you'll probably pass out unless you're one of those fighter pilots who train to withstand up to 5Gs.</p><p>Now, if you don't pass out, you may worry about the freezing temperatures up here.&#160; But, it turns out, your suit's more likely to melt than freeze. You know how you can warm your hands by rubbing them together?</p><p>Now imagine your supersuit rubbing against air molecules in the atmosphere at least 6 times the speed of sound. You'll heat up to about 1,650 ¬∫C ‚Äî hot enough to melt iron!</p><p>In fact, the heat is so intense, it strips electrons from their atoms forming a pink plasma around you that will ultimately destroy suit.</p><p>If that's not enough of a problem, the drag will rip off your limbs. But thankfully, Tony Stark has your back, and somehow, your supersuit holds with you intact.</p><p>At 41 km up you've now reached the world record for highest skydive. In 2014, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/alan-eustace-highest-altitude-jump-world-record-2014-10\">Alan Eustace</a> wore a pressurized space suit as he rode a balloon up to this height. He broke the sound barrier on his way down before deploying his parachute and landed about 15 minutes after the drop.</p><p>But you'll be falling much faster than Eustace ‚Äî about 3 times the speed of sound. So, in reality, you're not going to slow down enough to safely deploy your chute. That's where Iron Man can help us one last time. By 1 km up you've reached the territory of ordinary skydivers who don't need fancy suits to survive.</p><p>And at this point, your parachute can do its thing.&#160; And it's finally time to land softly.</p><p>Whew, what a ride! What sort of daring feat would you want us to try next? Let us know in the comments below. And thanks for watching.</p><p>A special thanks to <a href=\"https://wmich.edu/mechanical-aerospace/directory/brueshaber\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Shawn R Brueshaber</a>&#160;at Western Michigan University and&#160;<a href=\"http://science.hamptonu.edu/aps/faculty/sayanagi.cfm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Kunio Sayanagi</a>&#160;at Hampton University for their help with this video.</p><p><em>EDITOR'S NOTE: This video was originally published in July 2018.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a ultra-cold temperatures on its journey from the production line to a patient&#39;s arm.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Leon Neal/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Moderna on Monday said that its coronavirus vaccine works to prevent COVID-19.&#160;</li>\n<li>Moderna is now the second drugmaker to share positive results for a coronavirus vaccine after Pfizer said a week ago that its shot works.</li>\n<li>Pfizer's vaccine needs to be stored at negative 94 degrees Fahrenheit, presenting a challenge for vaccine distribution.</li>\n<li>Moderna's vaccine, however, is stable for up to a month at standard refrigeration temperatures, between 36 degrees Fahrenheit and 46 degrees Fahrenheit.</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-healthcare\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"2e12e8b76b1304c6cbd7ac1c8a5fa6c4\">For more stories like this, sign up here for Business Insider's daily healthcare newsletter.</a></li>\n</ul><p>Moderna on Monday said that its experimental vaccine was <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">effective at preventing COVID-19</a>, the disease caused by the novel coronavirus.</p><p>The findings come from a massive and well-designed study, but they haven't been reviewed by outside experts or by regulators. The news comes just one week after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">Pfizer shared that its vaccine was effective in preventing COVID-19</a>, sending markets soaring on the hope that an effective vaccine would help end the pandemic.&#160;</p><p>Moderna's shot comes with one crucial advantage over Pfizer's: It doesn't require a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vaccine-cold-chain-why-coronavirus-shot-needs-to-be-cold-2020-11\">deep-freeze</a>. Instead, the shot can be stored at standard refrigerator temperatures for up to a month, Moderna said on Monday.&#160;</p><p>Hospitals and health officials were working to figure out how to store and distribute Pfizer's shot, particularly in more rural areas, because the process can involve dry ice and special freezers. Some hospitals and city and state health officials were seeking <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-freezers-focus/u-s-states-race-to-buy-ultra-cold-vaccine-freezers-fueling-supply-worries-idUSKBN27T2S6\">to acquire the special freezers to store that shot, Reuters reported</a>.</p><h2>Pfizer's shot is stored at extremely cold temperatures&#160;</h2><p>Pfizer's vaccine needs to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/vaccine-cold-chain-why-coronavirus-shot-needs-to-be-cold-2020-11\">shipped and stored at negative 94 degrees Fahrenheit</a>, a temperature colder than what's needed for most other vaccines. That can be challenging in the US and presents even more of an obstacle in some other countries.&#160;</p><p>Pfizer will ship the vaccine by air and land using dry ice, along with reusable GPS temperature-monitoring devices.</p><p>Pfizer is<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-is-developing-powder-version-of-its-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-is-developing-powder-version-of-its-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">&#160;working on a next-generation version</a>&#160;of its shot that wouldn't need to kept at extremely cold temperatures, the company's chief scientific officer told Business Insider.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-is-developing-powder-version-of-its-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-is-developing-powder-version-of-its-covid-19-vaccine-2020-11\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Pfizer's top scientist tells us the&#160;</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">pharma</em><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">&#160;giant is already thinking about a new version of its coronavirus vaccine for 2021 that can overcome one of its biggest limitations</em></a></p><h2>Moderna's only requires standard refrigeration</h2><p>Moderna's vaccine, meanwhile, can be stored using standard refrigeration for up to 30 days, the company said on Monday. That greatly simplifies the distribution challenge compared to Pfizer's shot.</p><p>The shot is stable for a month at anywhere from 36 degrees Fahrenheit to 46 degrees Fahrenheit, which is the standard temperatures of refrigerators.&#160;</p><p>Moderna's vaccine can also be stored for up to six months at -4 degrees Fahrenheit, a typical temperature requirement that hospitals and clinics are used to.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a The more nutritious option will have 55% less saturated fat than traditional beef.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Beyond Burger is doubling down on nutrition with two new burgers.&#160;</p><p>On Monday, the plant-based \"meat\" maker announced it is rolling out two new versions of the Beyond Burger in early 2021. In a press release, the company classified one as the \"juiciest burger yet\" and the other as the \"most nutritious patty to date.\"&#160;</p><p>Beyond Meat and other plant-based protein makers have been grappling with how to best position themselves when it comes to nutrition.</p><p>While many people are interested in plant-based options for health reasons, meat-free options are often similar to the meat that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/beyond-burger-vs-impossible-burger-nutrition-compares-2019-6\">they are attempting to replicate in terms of calories and fat.&#160;</a></p><p>Plant-based options typically have far less cholesterol, but some actually have more sodium than meaty alternatives, according to<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/beyond-burger-vs-impossible-burger-nutrition-compares-2019-6\"> Business Insider's 2019 analysis.&#160;</a></p><p>However, plant-based \"meat\" makers like Beyond have the ability to refine their formula and continue to reinvent their products.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/beyond-meat-fast-food-future-2019-12\">Inside Beyond Meat's mission to take over fast food, from KFC's fried chicken to McDonald's burgers</a></em></p><p>The \"juicy\" new Beyond Burger will have 35% less saturated fat than a classic 80/20 beef burger patty. The more nutritious option will have 55% less saturated fat than beef.&#160;</p><p>\"Both new burgers will boast the same savory taste profile, have lower overall fat and fewer calories than 80/20 beef, and have B vitamins and minerals comparable to the micronutrient profile of beef,\" Beyond Meat said in a press release.&#160;</p><p>Beyond Meat did not release full nutrition information for the two new burgers. But, its new burgers highlight an advantage plant-based protein makers have on traditional meat companies: their ability to continue to improve nutritional info. Beyond Meat's chief growth officer, Chuck Muth, told Business Insider last year that the company's priorities are improving in three areas ‚Äî <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/beyond-meat-fast-food-future-2019-12\">nutrition, price, and taste.&#160;</a></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Fire TV and Fire tablets on Tuesday, Max announced on Monday.</p><p>Max launched in May <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-hbo-max-not-available-on-roku-amazon-fire-tv-2020-5\">amid a standoff with Amazon and Roku</a>, the two biggest streaming distribution platforms. Those two accounted for a combined 70% market share as of July 2019, according to the market research firm <a href=\"https://www.parksassociates.com/blog/article/amazon---roku-control-almost-70--of-the-us-streaming-player-market\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"9b6478182a24479920eeced799c5f0a9\">Parks Associates</a>.</p><p>A Max spokesperson told Business Insider that WarnerMedia is in discussions with Roku. Roku declined to comment.</p><p>NBCUniversal's new streaming platform, Peacock, also launched in July <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-peacock-not-available-on-roku-and-amazon-fire-tv-2020-7\">without a deal with Amazon or Roku</a>, but has since struck an agreement with Roku.</p><p>The general disagreements stemmed from the fact that WarnerMedia and NBCU wanted users to access their services directly through their apps, rather than through aggregation services like the Roku Channel or Amazon Channels.&#160;</p><p>Roku takes 20% and Amazon between 15% and 45% of subscription fees through these services, according to <a href=\"https://variety.com/2020/digital/news/hbo-max-peacock-roku-amazon-streaming-1234703977/\">Variety</a>, which reported in July that Roku and Amazon were also seeking ad inventory, free content for the Roku Channel and Amazon's IMDb TV, and more. A third of US customers subscribe to streamers through these services, according to Parks Associates.</p><p>In October, WarnerMedia's parents company AT&#38;T said that 8.6 million customers had activated HBO Max.</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li><h2>Read more about WarnerMedia and HBO Max</h2></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-warnermedia-layoffs-and-future-of-cnn-hbo-max-2020-11\">Inside WarnerMedia as huge layoffs hit the company and speculation swirls around the futures of CNN and HBO Max</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/warnermedia-new-layoffs-read-memo-from-ceo-jason-kilar-2020-11\">WarnerMedia has started a big new round of layoffs. src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fac645a98669500182b585a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"jones day law firm discrimination 4x3\" height=\"1800\" width=\"2400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jones Day; Samantha Lee/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Jones Day, the major law firm that made headlines this week&#160;<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/09/business/jones-day-trump-election-lawsuits.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"8fd38cb7a580bdecf8f687590d763c32\">when attorneys complained to The New York Times</a>&#160;about their employer's role in election-related litigation, is facing accusations of sexism in the workplace that, lawsuits say, led to unfair advantages for men.</p><p>Three federal lawsuits filed between 2016 and 2019 have contained claims of gender and pregnancy discrimination against the firm.</p><p>One, filed in April 2019, claims that the firm discriminates against women by paying them less than male peers, while another, brought by a married couple who once worked together at Jones Day, claims the firm does not give men and women the same amount of leave time after having a child.</p><p>A third, filed in 2018 by former partner Wendy Moore over wrongful termination and gender discrimination, was settled last year.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jones-day-pay-discrimination-pregnancy-gender-lawsuit-allegations-trump-election-2020-11?r=jonesday-teaser\">Business Insider found separate allegations</a> that have not been previously reported or filed in a suit. The findings are a result of interviews with dozens of people who have worked at the firm. The people who shared allegations did so on the condition of anonymity for fear of repercussions, though their identities are known to us.</p><p>Dave Petrou, senior manager of global public relations at Jones Day, did not respond to emails and follow-up phone calls about these previously unreported allegations.</p><h2><a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/11/15/business/walmart-customers-metering-coronavirus/index.html\">CNN</a> first reported Sunday.</p><p>Many US states have introduced <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/states-restrictions-surging-coronavirus-cases-2020-11\">travel and public gathering </a>controls in the run up to Thanksgiving, and some ‚Äî including Washington and Michigan, which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/washington-michigan-covid-19-lockdown-covid19-covid-rules-thanksgiving-2020-11\">on Sunday announced partial lockdowns</a> ‚Äî have placed restrictions on the capacity of stores.</p><p>Walmart first began restricting customer numbers <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-will-count-shoppers-limit-how-many-can-enter-2020-4\">in early April</a>. Stores were only allowed to reach 20% of their visitor capacity, though local guidelines could push this lower, and staff controlled how many customers could enter at a time.</p><p>Though the 20% limit remained in place, the retailer stopped counting the number of customers in early October, it told Business Insider. Stores rarely, if ever, breached the 20% mark even after they stopped counting, it said.</p><p>Over the weekend, it restarted monitoring again.</p><p>\"We know from months of metering data in our stores that the vast majority of the time our stores didn't reach our self-imposed 20% metering capacity,\" a Walmart spokesperson told Business Insider.</p><p>\"Out of an abundance of caution, we have resumed counting the number of people entering and leaving our stores.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/rei-workers-say-coops-black-friday-closure-is-marketing-move-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">REI gives its employees a paid day off on Black Friday, but hourly workers say that it's a 'marketing move' and that the company has strayed from its co-op roots</a></em></p><p>Walmart has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-black-friday-stores-limited-capacity-3-day-event-2020-10\">also revised its Black Friday offering</a> to make it \"safer and more manageable for both our customers and our associates\" amid the pandemic, it said in October.</p><p>The retailer is launching its deals over three separate days, two of which have already happened, and it will release offers online at least two days before they hit stores.</p><p>Walmart will also limit the number of Black Friday shoppers to just 20% of store capacity. Customers will have to form a line to enter the store, and staff will sanitize shopping carts and remind customers to wear masks.</p><p>COVID-19 cases across the US have been spiraling as the country is hit by a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-surge-is-tsunami-comparison-spring-summer-2020-11\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"cc7b69b4c1c0f98a30c6d1fd3261a688\">third wave of the virus</a>.</p><p>In the week to November 16, the US recorded a record 1 million new COVID-19 cases, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-cases-breaks-record-trump-tweets-unproven-voter-fraud-2020-11\">bringing its total to 11 million cases</a>.
