00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Emily Murphy, the official blocking Biden's transition, has a record of working the system in ways that benefit Trump, ethics expert says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/gsa-official-emily-murphy-track-record-of-trump-partisanship-schaub-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb27d3d1c741f0019ac9ecd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"emily murphy GSA trump\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Emily Murphy is sworn in as head of the General Services Administration in December 2017.\n<p class=\"copyright\">GSA/handout via Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A former director of the US Office of Government Ethics accused Emily Murphy, head of the GSA, of being a \"partisan loyalist\" determined to help President Donald Trump.</li>\n<li>The GSA is the part of the US government which authorizes the start of a presidential transition. Murphy has not yet done so in the wake of Joe Biden's election victory.</li>\n<li>Walter Schaub Jr made his charge against Murphy <a href=\"https://www.nybooks.com/daily/2020/11/13/the-presidential-transition-meets-murphys-law/\">in the New York Review of Books</a>, highlighting her apparent partisanship.</li>\n<li>This is not an outlier, he wrote, describing two other episodes of Murphy's work at the GSA which he said appear to have been hand-in-glove with Trump.</li>\n<li>Neither Murphy nor the GSA immediately responded to Business Insider's request for comment.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The General Services Administration (GSA) official who is holding up the transition of President-elect Joe Biden has a long history of pro-Trump partisanship, a former government ethics director has said.</p><p>Walter Shaub, who was Director of the US Office of Government Ethics between 2013-17, accused GSA head Emily Murphy of seemingly \"putting her loyalty to Trump over her duty to the American people\" <a href=\"https://www.nybooks.com/daily/2020/11/13/the-presidential-transition-meets-murphys-law/\">in a scathing article for The New York Review of Books</a>.</p><p>Murphy, an appointee of President Donald Trump, is the GSA official charged with formally recognizing the victor in a US presidential election, which allows a formal transition process to begin.</p><p>This nod from the GSA releases resources to ensure a smooth transition for the President-elect, including, according to Schaub, $6.3 million in funds, office space, and key briefings.</p><p>But Murphy, who as a political appointee Schaub alleges is held on a \"tight leash\" by Trump, has not budged while the president continues to baselessly dispute the outcome of the election.&#160;</p><p>Biden <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trumps-refusal-concede-could-mean-biden-cant-national-security-information-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">has continued to press ahead</a> with without access to the briefings and resources the GSA can offer.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/12/ron-klain-transition-coronavirus-vaccine-436411\">Biden's chief of staff has criticized the decision</a>, which he says harms the President-elect's ability to handle challenges like the coronavirus pandemic.</p><p>Schaub alleged that Murphy's stance is not an outlier, but part of a pattern of partisan behavior that has worked the system apparently in Trump's favor.&#160;</p><p>Schaub gave two examples:</p><ul><li><strong>He accused Murphy of being part of a Trump administration power grab to weaken the civil service.</strong></li></ul><p>The Trump administration has been <a href=\"https://www.afge.org/article/trump-administration-moves-to-abolish-opm-despite-law-prohibiting-it/\">pushing to abolish</a> the Office of Personnel Management (OPM) and put it under the GSA's control.</p><p>Schaub characterized the move as a power grab that would put government employees under added political pressure.</p><p>The Trump administration abandoned plans to abolish the OPM the day before Election Day, <a href=\"https://www.federaltimes.com/management/2020/11/02/trump-administration-abandons-plan-to-split-up-personnel-office/\">according to Federal Times</a>.&#160;</p><ul><li><strong>He said Murphy axed plans to move FBI's Washington headquarters in a way that protected Trump's outside business interests<br></strong></li></ul><p>The FBI's move from an ageing building in central DC could have harmed the Trump International Hotel, Schaub wrote.</p><p>His logic was that, once vacated, the FBI building could have been turned into a rival business and hurt Trump's bottom line.</p><p>Murphy met with Trump not long before the decision, but refused to discuss it when asked about it by the GSA's inspector general, Schaub wrote.</p><p>Neither Murphy nor the GSA immediately responded to Business Insider's request for comment.&#160;</p><p>Schaub has also encouraged the general public on Twitter to call the GSA and ask why Murphy has not released transition resources.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Walter Shaub  (@waltshaub) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1328072329482670086?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 15, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Schaub noted the contrast in Trump's approach compared to 2008, when he was told by a George W. Bush administration official that they wanted to create the \"nicest transition in history\" for then-President-elect Obama.&#160;</p><p>\"At this point, it is difficult to imagine Republican leaders repeating the words,\" he wrote.&#160;</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.nybooks.com/daily/2020/11/13/the-presidential-transition-meets-murphys-law/\">Read the full article here at The New York Review of Books.&#160;</a></h2><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/-LiebUDD2Lk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 16 Nov 2020 15:47:02 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fb28562402d49001924f136?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"2aa470186057bfaf75db2c35b5b3ba48","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn9@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-20-105_ddb470bc1c3192a7.webp","destWidth":1141,"destHeight":856,"sourceBytes":45120,"destBytes":45120,"author":"mjankowicz@businessinsider.com (Mia Jankowicz)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb27d3d1c741f0019ac9ecd?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-26-132_ac89a47b0165997a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=-LiebUDD2Lk:-SSlTVpLHTk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn12@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-25-866_10a12f3286b3da5d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=-LiebUDD2Lk:-SSlTVpLHTk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn7@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-26-430_e51ae7c5df22aad6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=-LiebUDD2Lk:-SSlTVpLHTk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn87@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-46-26-289_13b8e8c33ec7050c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/-LiebUDD2Lk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn100@2020_3/2020/11/16/16-46-24-117_e69a10f600cda3a1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138283},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"As someone with a disability, Biden's inclusion of 'disability' in his victory speech was monumental","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/bidens-inclusion-disability-community-victory-speech-monumental-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faef19d1c741f0019ac9c73?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Biden-victory\" height=\"3267\" width=\"4357\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In President-elect Joe Biden&#39;s victory speech, he acknowledged the disability community.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Andrew Harnik-Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Obama gave me hope as a disabled person, but the tangible benefits for the disability community were not very extensive.</li>\n<li>President-elect Joe Biden mentioned the disability community in his victory speech, which is monumental and encouraging.</li>\n<li>A Biden presidency will be a well-needed respite from Trump's continued attacks on disability and healthcare.</li>\n<li>Sarah Kim is a freelance journalist and writer with cerebral palsy.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>At the tender age of 13, my eyes grew misty on the night that President Barack Obama was elected the first Black president of the United States. Growing up in a predominately white suburban town, I had yet to add the term \"person of color\" to my vocabulary.</p><p>I had yet to realize that I, a daughter of Korean-American immigrants, belong in such a group ‚Äì it would take me another seven years to finally realize that Asian Americans are, indeed, considered people of color. Nonetheless, even as a na√≠ve teenager, I could still recognize the magnitude of President Obama's achievement.</p><p>Not only was I one of the few Asian Americans in my K-12 school, I was also the only kid with a physical disability in my classes. I have <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/ncbddd/cp/facts.html\">cerebral palsy</a>, which affects my speech and mobility; I've used a wheelchair for most of my life. So, I truly resonated with the significance of then-newly elected President Obama being in a position where no one who looked like him had been before.</p><p>However, it would take another 12 years for me to feel seen by the highest office in the land. On November 7, President-elect <a href=\"https://www.huffpost.com/entry/joe-biden-disability-advocates-express-joy_n_5fa83941c5b66009569bb896\">Joe Biden mentioned the word \"disability\"</a> in his victory speech, which was only the second time in modern history (with available transcripts of election night speeches) that a president or president-elect has acknowledged this community specifically in a victory speech (apart from President Obama in both <a href=\"https://millercenter.org/the-presidency/presidential-speeches/november-4-2008-remarks-election-night\">2008</a> and <a href=\"https://millercenter.org/the-presidency/presidential-speeches/november-6-2012-2012-election-night-victory-speech\">2012</a>):</p><p><em>\"We must make the promise of the country real for everybody, no matter their race, their ethnicity, their faith, their identity, or their disability.\"</em></p><p>Even <a href=\"https://twitter.com/i/status/1325279155521527808\">CNN host Jake Tapper acknowledged</a> Biden's inclusion of the word. But this moment did not come easily or quickly, and credit is due to all the people on the ground who made it happen.</p><h2>It's been a hard four years for the disability community</h2><p>In 2016, like millions of others, I watched as President Donald Trump won the presidency. I was an aspiring journalist at that time, and after <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2016-election/trump-s-worst-offense-mocking-disabled-reporter-poll-finds-n627736\">witnessing Trump openly mock</a> a broadcast reporter with a disability, my outlook on the four years to come was grim.</p><p>Nevertheless, I forged ahead ‚Äì I completed my master's program at Columbia Journalism School and never looked back. In my nearly three years of being a diversity and inclusion journalist, I experienced firsthand the vast underrepresentation of the disability community both in media and inside the industry itself. And I've made it my lifelong goal to amplify their voices through my work.</p><p>People with disabilities constitute the nation's largest minority group, <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/ncbddd/disabilityandhealth/infographic-disability-impacts-all.html\">making up nearly 26%</a> ‚Äì or 61 million ‚Äì Americans ages 18 and older. And unlike any other minority group, disability transcends across all identities: gender, race, socioeconomic class, religion, nationality, and sexuality. So, every issue and policy affects people with disabilities often to greater extents than other minority groups. Especially in 2020, the problems at center stage are disproportionately affecting people with disabilities: from<a href=\"https://thehill.com/blogs/congress-blog/politics/524973-regardless-of-party-the-next-congress-must-prioritize-disability\"> healthcare</a> to<a href=\"https://news.vanderbilt.edu/2020/11/04/new-research-documents-how-covid-19-multiplies-stress-and-trauma-for-people-with-disabilities/\"> coronavirus</a> to<a href=\"https://www.cavalierdaily.com/article/2020/11/covid-19-amplifies-challenges-for-those-with-disabilities-chronic-illnesses\"> access to education</a> and<a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/andrewpulrang/2020/10/30/10-questions-disabled-americans-should-ask-themselves-before-voting/?sh=7bae5c393419\"> unemployment</a>.</p><p>Frustrated with the lack of representation, disability rights advocates Gregg Beratan, Andrew Pulrang, and Alice Wong founded the <a href=\"http://cripthevote.blogspot.com/\">#CripTheVote</a> social media movement. The movement aims to activate and engage disabled people on policies and practices essential to the disability community. It is grounded in online conversations encouraging individual and collective action in the face of inequality, ableism, and oppression in all forms.</p><p>Over the four years of Trump's presidency, he seems to take every opportunity to harm the disability community. For example, his administration made the already-tumultuous Social Security Disability Insurance <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/sarahkim/2019/12/17/trump-administrations-proposed-ssdi-policy-change/?sh=508dd7934abe\">application even more complicated</a>, <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/a35d8a/trump-is-now-going-to-make-life-hell-for-immigrants-with-disabilities\">denied visas and green cards to immigrants with disabilities</a> who need government assistance, and attempted to <a href=\"https://www.disabilityscoop.com/2019/05/10/trump-administration-appeal-special-ed-ruling/26606/\">cut budgets for special education</a>. Not to mention that repealing the Affordable Care Act, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/courts_law/supreme-court-affordable-care-act/2020/11/09/d7adbbf4-22a1-11eb-a688-5298ad5d580a_story.html\">which the Trump administration has attempted</a>, would make millions of Americans with <a href=\"https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/disability/news/2020/10/09/491428/repealing-aca-create-chaos-disability-community-pandemic/\">disabilities lose access to affordable health insurance</a>. Needless to say, it's been a fearful and stressful couple of years for the disability community.</p><p>Which is why Biden's inclusion of our community in his victory speech was the light at the end of the tunnel we desperately needed. While the acknowledgment lasted for a split second in his whole speech, it made Americans with disabilities ‚Äî including myself ‚Äî feel seen in such a significant way. Throughout history, especially for the past four years, people with disabilities have been forced to set the bar very low. However, Biden's inclusion of our community in his speech has offered us a glimmer of hope and recognition that we have been looking for all along. He has even designated a <a href=\"https://joebiden.com/covid19-disabilities/\">specific disability-inclusion component</a> in his COVID-19 relief plans and laid out a detailed plan to ensure the <a href=\"https://joebiden.com/disabilities/\">advancement of people with disabilities in all sectors of life</a>.</p><p>Throughout his presidential campaign, Biden has been open about his<a href=\"https://www.health.com/mind-body/joe-biden-stutter\"> own speech disability</a> and shamelessly embraced and accepted <a href=\"https://www.vogue.com/article/hunter-biden-struggles-with-addiction-remind-me-of-my-own\">his son Hunter's addiction and mental health issues</a>. President Franklin D. Roosevelt was the <a href=\"https://www.fdrlibrary.org/polio\">only US president who used a wheelchair</a>, but he <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-fdr-hid-his-paralysis-from-american-public-even-while-campaigning-2019-4\">deliberately hid his disability</a> ‚Äì paralysis from polio ‚Äì from the public. It took until 2020, but it is so refreshing to finally have a president who both acknowledges the disability community and is honest with his own disability. I am hopeful that because of this, Biden will include people with disabilities in his policy development and the overall presidential term.</p><p><em>Sarah Kim is a freelance journalist and writer with cerebral palsy. Her work focuses on diversity, equity, and inclusion, and she has written for TIME, Betches, Teen Vogue, Glamour, I Weigh, Forbes, Greatist, and more. Links to her work can be found at <a href=\"http://www.beingsarahkim.com\">www.beingsarahkim.com</a>.&#160;</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Josh Ostrovsky, aka The Fat Jewish, is a case study in turning social influence into a booming business. Here's how he grew a 10 million-follower Instagram account and sold his wine company to Anheuser-Busch InBev.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-social-media-influencers-can-learn-from-the-fat-jewish-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa07e8e69331a0011bc6da1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Josh Ostrovsky\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ostrovsky&#39;s breakout moment came in 2013, when he posted a video of himself conducting a spin class for the homeless using New York City&#39;s bike-sharing system Citi Bike.\n<p class=\"copyright\">(Photo by Santiago Felipe/Getty Images)</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Josh Ostrovsky, known professionally as The Fat Jewish, has turned his loyal 10.6 million Instagram followers into energized customers.&#160;</li>\n<li>Last year he sold his wine company, Babe Wine, to Anheuser-Busch InBev. It was the brewing behemoth's largest investment in wine.</li>\n<li>Business Insider spoke with three social media management founders and CEOs, all of whom said Ostrovsky's success is replicable for other influencers &#8212; provided they take the right steps.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Memeing the Kardashians and judging a wet T-shirt contest for pregnant women doesn't sound like the normal start to entrepreneurial ventures. But Josh Ostrovsky ‚Äî better known by his social-media alias, The Fat Jewish ‚Äî isn't typical.</p><p>Instead of filling fans' feeds with photos of chiseled abs and dewy skin, Ostrovsky, 38, serves up to <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/thefatjewish/?hl=en\">his 10.6 million Instagram followers</a> photos of his pronounced belly and his upright ponytail, which he affectionately refers to as a \"<a href=\"https://twitter.com/FATJEW/status/727279337536389122?s=20\">hair erection</a>.\"</p><p>Over the past eight years, Ostrovsky has ascended from viral hit to legitimate businessman. He's landed sponsorships with prominent companies like Burger King, appeared in beloved TV shows and a music video, and partnered with celebrities like Madonna. Perhaps most notably, in 2015, he cofounded Babe Wine, which he sold to Anheuser-Busch InBev in 2019 in what the brewer says was its largest wine investment to date.</p><p>Ostrovsky has also said that the influencer world has become so competitive in the past eight years that his playbook for netting high-price sponsorship deals is already obsolete.&#160;</p><p>But Business Insider spoke with social-media experts who agreed that Ostrovsky's success is indeed replicable for other influencers, provided they follow a few key steps: Build a strong persona, remain authentic, and understand the needs and wants of their followers.</p><h2><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-fat-jewish-built-an-empire-off-instagram-and-jokes-2020-11?r=fatjewish-teaser\" Alexander/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Airlines, cruises, and hotels all traded higher on Monday as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">encouraging results</a> from Moderna's vaccine trial boosted the so-called reopening trade.</strong></li><li><strong>Moderna announced Monday morning that its experimental coronavirus vaccine was 94.5% effective at preventing COVID-19 in trial patients.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ual-stock\">United Airlines</a>&#160;jumped as much as 8.6%.&#160;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aal-stock\">American Airlines</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/dal-stock\">Delta</a>&#160;both gained roughly 6%.</strong></li><li><strong>Cruises stocks rallied more than 8%, while <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mar-stock\">Mariott International</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/hlt-stock\">Hilton Hotels</a> also saw strong gains.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestutm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\">Visit the Business Insider homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Airline, hotel, and cruise stocks surged on Monday as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mrna-stock\">Moderna's</a> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">encouraging vaccine trial results</a> spurred fresh optimism for an end to the coronavirus pandemic.</p><p>The biotech company announced Monday morning that its experimental coronavirus vaccine was 94.5% effective at preventing COVID-19 in a preliminary analysis. The update comes one week after <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pfe-stock\">Pfizer</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/bntx-stock\">BioNTech</a> revealed <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">similarly positive results</a> from early trials of their own vaccine. While both candidates still need to receive approval from the US Food and Drug Administration, their supposed effectiveness suggests a nationwide rollout could come in 2021.&#160;</p><p>The news boosted shares of companies hit hardest by the virus and stay-at-home restrictions. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ual-stock\">United Airlines</a>&#160;leaped as much as 8.6%.&#160;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aal-stock\">American Airlines</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/dal-stock\">Delta</a>&#160;both jumped roughly 6% shortly after the vaccine news.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-cheap-companies-value-economic-rebound-goldman-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 20 deeply underpriced stocks now before the recovery helps them rebound and crush Wall Street's low expectations in 2021</a></em></p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/rcl-stock\">Royal Caribbean Cruises</a>&#160;soared 8% at intraday highs. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ccl-stock\">Carnival</a>&#160;and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nclh-stock\">Norwegian Cruise Line Holdings</a> gained as much as 10%.</p><p>Hotels also rallied on the news.&#160;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/h-stock\">Hyatt Hotels</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mar-stock\">Marriott International</a>&#160;gained as much as 5.9% and 4.6%, respectively. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/hlt-stock\">Hilton Hotels</a>&#160;traded as much as 3.7% higher.&#160;</p><p>The moves mimic the dislocations seen after previous encouraging vaccine updates. Stocks that would benefit the most from a full economic recovery bounce higher, while those that thrived through the pandemic slide. Monday was no different, as stay-at-home stocks such as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/zm-stock\">Zoom</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pton-stock\">Peloton</a> all traded lower.</p><p>Both Moderna and Pfizer aim to apply for emergency use authorization later this month. Approval would allow the companies to quickly begin distributing their vaccines to the most vulnerable populations. Even if both candidates are approved by regulators, vaccine supply is set to be very limited.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-tips-for-success-william-danoff-shares-market-beating-guide-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Peter Lynch disciple William Danoff manages over $124 billion and has beaten the market for 30 years. He shares the 10 investment rules that ensured his success.</a></em></p><p>Still, new hopes for a near-term breakthrough <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-sp500-near-records-moderna-vaccine-data-2020-11-1029806741\">lifted the broader stock market</a>. The Dow Jones industrial average opened 375 points higher and closed in on an all-time high. The&#160;Nasdaq composite erased early gains underperformed peer indexes as major tech names fell.</p><p>Oil futures extended gains as traders hoped for a vaccine to revive travel-based consumption. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">West Texas Intermediate crude</a> contracts gained as much as 4.9%, to $42.09 per barrel.</p><p><em><strong>Now read more markets coverage from Markets Insider and Business Insider:</strong></em></p><p><em><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/market-strategy-5-trade-tips-kolanovic-coronavirus-vaccine-rotation-jpm-2020-11-1029803373\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">JPMorgan's quant chief shares 5 trade recommendations following Pfizer's vaccine 'game-changer'</a></strong></em></p><p><em><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-sentiment-falls-surging-covid19-cases-concern-economic-recovery-umich-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"5\" data-analytics-module=\"\">US consumer sentiment falls for the first time in 4 months as spiking COVID-19 cases spur worry</a></strong></em></p><p><em><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/noelle-cazalis-investing-strategy-rathbones-ethical-bond-fund2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"4\" data-analytics-module=\"\">The manager of Rathbones' $2.4 billion Ethical Bond Fund is beating her benchmark ‚Äì and 95% of her peers. (Ben Winck)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fb273cf1c741f0019ac9ebb?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn16@2020_3/2020/11/16/16-46-23-695_949240a3ed09b701.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=jA5UqnBJ2cQ:KBpNX-dYc0s:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn59@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-23-693_b40415c8c9f4b91a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=jA5UqnBJ2cQ:KBpNX-dYc0s:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn79@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-096_6bf8c2577cca26ee.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=jA5UqnBJ2cQ:KBpNX-dYc0s:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn84@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-22-654_e41d4eb32ee026b2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/jA5UqnBJ2cQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn28@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-25-851_520196b11b6db116.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138338},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"The man in charge of evaluating coronavirus vaccines for the FDA lays out why it will take weeks to vet a COVID-19 shot","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/fdas-peter-marks-on-the-coronavirus-vaccine-review-process-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3fcfc042f43f001ddfe41b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Peter Marks\" height=\"683\" width=\"910\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>FDA&#39;s Dr. Peter Marks\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/dr-peter-marks-the-director-of-the-center-for-biologics-news-photo/1228010056?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Amanda Andrade-Rhoades/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>As coronavirus vaccines inch closer to reality, the man in charge of reviewing the approval applications wants Americans to trust the process.</li>\n<li>That means we're not going to get surprise Food and Drug Administration approvals in the coming days, despite two COVID-19 vaccine frontrunners announcing success over the past week.</li>\n<li>The review process will be measured in weeks, Dr. Peters Marks, director of the FDA's center for biological products, told Business Insider on Friday.</li>\n<li>\"Everything that we are trying to do here, this is all about ensuring the public re-develops the kind of trust they once had in vaccines,\" Marks said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"http://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/insider-healthcare\">For more stories like this, sign up here for Business Insider's daily healthcare newsletter.</a></li>\n</ul><p>The man in charge of reviewing the applications for coronavirus vaccine candidates has a clear message for the American public: Trust the process.</p><p>It'll play out before your eyes over the next few weeks.&#160;</p><p>\"Look at the process that we're following,\" Dr. Peter Marks, the leader of the Food and Drug Administration's biologics center, said in a Friday phone interview with Business insider. \"We're going to have a very open process.\"</p><p>While the coronavirus pandemic rages across the country as it never has before, the hopes for a vaccine that can pull society out of this crisis have strengthened in recent days.</p><p>The pharmaceutical giant Pfizer and its German partner BioNTech said on November 9 its vaccine candidate <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">was more than 90% effective</a> at preventing COVID-19 in an interim analysis of a massive clinical study. The upstart Massachusetts biotech Moderna <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">said Monday its two-dose regimen was 94.5% effective</a>, according to preliminary results from a late-stage trial.</p><p>But the intense effort to develop a COVID-19 shot in record time has left many Americans feeling uneasy about the quick timeline. <a href=\"https://www.statnews.com/pharmalot/2020/11/10/harris-poll-covid19-vaccine-masks-distancing/\">Recent</a> <a href=\"https://www.consumerreports.org/vaccines/covid-19-vaccine-answers-start-to-arrive-but-americans-still-have-concerns/\">surveys</a> have shown an increasing number of Americans are hesitant to get a COVID-19 shot.&#160;</p><p>It's ultimately up to the FDA to decide whether it will authorize the experimental coronavirus vaccines, and the vetting process is expected to take weeks, Marks said. By taking time rather than rushing to an authorization, the hope is to build up more conviction in the final products.</p><p>\"What we need here is confidence,\" Marks said. \"Everything that we are trying to do here, this is all about ensuring the public re-develops the kind of trust they once had in vaccines.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-development-inside-the-lab-ceo-interview-2020-3\">'</a></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-development-inside-the-lab-ceo-interview-2020-3\">Crazy hours, short nights': The inside story of how a buzzy biotech upstart developed a potential coronavirus vaccine in record time</a></em></p><h2>'We have to take the amount of time that we need to take'</h2><p>Despite the encouraging reports, the data still has to be scrutinized before any shot is rolled out to the public.</p><p>That's where Marks comes in as the director of the FDA's Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research. He'll be overseeing the coronavirus vaccine review process, and said he is intent on running a transparent process to build trust.</p><p>Even amid a surging pandemic with rising levels of infections, hospitalizations, and deaths in the US, Marks is sticking to the steps.</p><p>That is, don't hold your breath for an overnight FDA approval or emergency OK for Pfizer or Moderna. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb29d8b402d49001924f1a5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FDA Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research Director Dr. Peter Marks\" height=\"2737\" width=\"3650\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Peter Marks, director of the FDA&#39;s Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research\n<p class=\"copyright\">FDA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Marks said said it would take \"weeks\" to review any vaccine application.</p><p>\"We have to take the amount of time that we need to take,\" Marks said. \"The caveat here with saying this word 'weeks' is there are situations whereby the quality of what comes in and the complexity of what comes in will determine how long it will take to do a review that we can feel very confident in.\"</p><p>If that vetting process isn't followed, Marks said he would resign from the agency.&#160;</p><p>\"You will see me leave if somebody said 'we're not going to look at the data, just get the thing approved,'\" he said.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/insider-pfizer-biontech-historic-coronavirus-vaccine-program-2020-11\">How the pharma giant Pfizer teamed up with a little-known biotech to develop an effective coronavirus vaccine in record time</a></em></p><h2>A long regulatory road ahead, with the goal of building public trust</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3adc16a3eafa001de068d8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vaccine\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Steve Parsons-WPA Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Before a vaccine is approved, companies have to submit it to the FDA for review.&#160;</p><p>Neither Moderna or Pfizer have even submitted an application for emergency use authorization (EUA) to regulators yet. Both companies are still collecting the required safety information from trial participants and anticipate submitting to the FDA in the next couple weeks.</p><p>From there, the FDA has its own process to follow. Career scientists will pore over the data and ultimately make a recommendation to authorize a vaccine. The agency will also consult a group of independent experts to share their advice.&#160;</p><p>This expert panel, known as an advisory committee, will take some time to set up, Marks said. The FDA needs time to prepare briefing documents that summarize the data and set the agenda for the panel's meeting.&#160;</p><p>\"I can't give you an exact timing, but it's going to be a matter of weeks between when we get a submission and having an AdComm,\" Marks said.</p><p>This isn't bureaucratic red tape ‚Äî the advisory committee meeting is one of the public's best views into the review process. The group will pick apart the data in a publicly broadcasted meeting and ultimately vote on whether or not to authorize the shot.&#160;</p><p>\"They'll hear some of the warts, as well as some of the benefits,\" Marks said on what the public could expect. \"I think that is actually what truth looks like. I think actually people are better than we think at seeing what the truth really is and recognizing that.\"</p><p>The FDA's own review will then carry on, taking into consideration the expert panel's perspective. The agency isn't required to follow the expert panels' recommendations, but often does so.&#160;</p><p>Now that the vaccine frontrunners appear to be highly effective, all eyes will soon turn to the FDA for the next steps. Marks said the agency is ready for the challenge that lies ahead.</p><p>\"We feel motivated ourselves to move as quickly as we possibly can,\" Marks said. \"This is not coming from anyone outside of the agency or inside of the agency except ourselves, because we understand how important this is.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Moderna plans to apply for emergency use authorization later this month.</strong></li><li><strong>The Dow Jones industrial average hit an intraday record, while the S&#38;P 500 traded less than 1% from its own all-time high.</strong></li><li><strong>The news specifically lifted so-called reopening stocks including airlines, hotels, and cruises.</strong></li><li><strong>Stay-at-home plays such as <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/zm-stock\">Zoom</a>&#160;and&#160;<a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a> tumbled.</strong></li><li><strong>Oil prices surged as investors bet on vaccine distribution to revive market demand. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">West Texas Intermediate crude</a> gained as much as 4.9%, to $42.09 per barrel.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/indices\">Watch major indexes update live here</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>US stocks rallied on Monday after <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/mrna-stock\">Moderna</a> announced its coronavirus vaccine candidate <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11\">reliably protected patients from COVID-19</a>. The Dow Jones industrial average hit an intraday record, while the S&#38;P 500 traded less than 1% from its own all-time high.</p><p>The biotech company said Monday morning that its experimental vaccine was 94.5% effective at preventing COVID-19 in trial patients. An independent group of experts found signs of effectiveness after reviewing data from an ongoing 30,000-person trial, Moderna said. The company plans to apply for emergency use authorization later this month.</p><p>The encouraging news comes one week after <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pfe-stock\">Pfizer</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/btnx-stock\">BioNTech</a> revealed similarly positive results from their own vaccine trial. While both experimental drugs still require regulatory approval to be distributed, their effectiveness suggests the virus could be reliably contained sooner than expected.</p><p><strong>Here's where US indexes stood at 11:35 a.m. ET on Monday:</strong></p><ul><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S&#38;P 500</a>:</strong> 3,624.57, up 1.1%</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/dow_jones?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dow Jones industrial average</a>:</strong> 29,931.67, up 1.5% (452 points)</li><li><strong><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nasdaq_composite?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nasdaq composite</a>:</strong> 11,905.31, up 0.6%</li></ul><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-cheap-companies-value-economic-rebound-goldman-2020-11\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 20 deeply underpriced stocks now before the recovery helps them rebound and crush Wall Street's low expectations in 2021</a></em></p><p>The so-called <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/airline-cruise-stocks-moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-data-market-reopening-recovery-2020-11-1029806318\">reopening trade soared</a> as Moderna's update lifted investor optimism. Airlines including <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ual-stock\">United</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aal-stock\">American</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/dal-stock\">Delta</a> gained, as did cruise lines. Hotel stocks also jumped as investors bet on near-term vaccine distribution to revive the beleaguered sector.</p><p>Conversely, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/zoom-peloton-wfh-stock-prices-moderna-covid-vaccine-trial-2020-11-1029806091\">stocks that thrived in the stay-at-home economy sank</a> as investors positioned for a full recovery. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/zm-stock\">Zoom</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pton-stock\">Peloton</a>, among others, tumbled. Falling tech giants in particular led the Nasdaq composite to underperform peer indexes.</p><p>\"The global population couldn't have asked for more from the Moderna vaccine,\" Seema Shah, chief strategist at Principal Global Investors, said. \"Visibility towards a return to normality is increasing, and this should provide more fuel to the reflation rally, with small caps, value, and cyclicals clear beneficiaries.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-how-peter-kraus-built-firm-where-to-invest-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Former AllianceBernstein CEO Peter Kraus outlines how he has built his disruptive boutique from a 'concept' into a 50-person, $3 billion firm in just 2 years ‚Äî and shares the 3 areas he is looking at for investing opportunities</a></em></p><p>Moderna's update offset concerns about still-rising COVID-19 cases throughout the US. The country reported more than 139,000 new cases on Sunday along with nearly 69,000 new hospitalizations, according to <a href=\"https://covidtracking.com/data\">The COVID Tracking Project</a>. Multiple cities have reinstated economic restrictions to hinder the virus's spread. With the pace of economic recovery already slowing, prolonged lockdowns risk freezing the nation's rebound.</p><p>Monday's strong open comes after Pfizer's own vaccine announcement spurred a massive rotation to value stocks throughout last week. Major indexes notched <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-vaccine-coronavirus-hopes-offset-virus-spike-2020-11-1029802604\">a second-straight weekly gain</a>&#160;as investors bet on near-term vaccine distribution.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stocks-buy-stay-at-home-stock-picks-post-pandemic-barclays-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Barclays details its ultimate strategy for picking stay-at-home market winners for a post-COVID world ‚Äî and shares 2 stocks all investors should own before the recovery accelerates</a></em></p><p>Spot <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/gold-price\">gold</a> fell slightly after hitting an intraday low of $1,865.30 per ounce as investors rotated out of safe-haven assets. The US dollar declined against most major currency peers and Treasury yields climbed.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Bitcoin</a> hovered around $16,400 as its recent rally cooled. The world's most popular cryptocurrency <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-16000-cryptocurrency-market-rally-btc-highest-years-paypal-2020-11-1029796564\">surged above the $16,000 resistance level</a> on Thursday as its fall rally pushed forward.</p><p>Oil prices gained on hopes for a vaccine to revive travel activity and overall consumption. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">West Texas Intermediate crude</a> surged as much as 4.9%, to $42.09 per barrel. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestarkets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"Washington and Michigan are entering partial lockdowns as COVID-19 cases in the states ‚Äî and nationwide ‚Äî spike","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/washington-michigan-covid-19-lockdown-covid19-covid-rules-thanksgiving-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2597b1c741f0019ac9e97?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Whitmer, Inslee\" height=\"2249\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Michigan Governor Gretchen Whitmer and Washington Governor Jay Inslee are putting their states into partial lockdowns this week.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rebecca Cook/Reuters, John Moore/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Governors for Michigan and Washington announced Sunday that their states will enter partial lockdowns this week.</li>\n<li>Both will ban most indoor social gatherings, such as in-person dining and movie theaters.</li>\n<li>In Washington, gyms must also close. In Michigan, high schools and colleges must bring all teaching online.</li>\n<li>Michigan's three-week lockdown starts midnight at the end of Tuesday, and Washington's four-week lockdown starts midnight at the end of Monday.</li>\n<li>Both states are experiencing rapid rises in COVID-19 cases.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Michigan and Washington are entering partial lockdowns to try to curb a spike of COVID-19 cases.</p><p>Both states will ban most indoor social gatherings, such as in-person dining and visits to movie theaters. Stores and services such as hairdressers will only be able to operate at limited capacity.</p><p>Michigan's three-week lockdown starts midnight at the end of Tuesday, and Washington's four-week lockdown starts midnight at the end of Monday.</p><p>Other states have introduced <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/states-restrictions-surging-coronavirus-cases-2020-11\">travel and public gathering restrictions</a> in the run up to Thanksgiving.</p><p>COVID-19 cases across the US have been spiraling as the country is hit by a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-surge-is-tsunami-comparison-spring-summer-2020-11\">third wave of the virus</a>.</p><p>In the week to November 16, the US recorded 1 million new COVID-19 cases, including 170,333 on Friday alone, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-cases-breaks-record-trump-tweets-unproven-voter-fraud-2020-11\">breaking the single-day count for the fourth day in a row</a>, according to data from <a href=\"https://covidtracking.com/data/national\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"abbdeb1bfbd9b97e70981657256dd06a\">The COVID Tracking Project. </a></p><p>This has brought its total to 11 million cases ‚Äî almost 20% of all worldwide cases recorded since the first case of the virus in late 2019. It is the world's highest tally.</p><h2>Michigan's new partial COVID-19 lockdown</h2><p>From Wednesday, restaurants won't be allowed to offer indoor dining, colleges and high schools must shift to online learning, and movie theaters and casinos have to shut.</p><p>Hospital admissions related to COVID-19 are rising dramatically in the state, and thousands of new cases are being added every day, <a href=\"https://www.michigan.gov/mdhhs/0,5885,7-339--545138--,00.html\">the Michigan Department of Health and Human Services (MDHHS) said Sunday</a> when it announced the new restrictions.</p><p>During the new lockdown, residents are only allowed to invite one other household to their home at a time.</p><p>Gyms and swimming pools will remain open for individual exercise at 25% capacity, but group exercise classes will be banned.</p><p>However, meeting outside as a group of up to 25, dining outdoors, and visiting parks will still be allowed.</p><p>Public transport, non-essential shops, and hairdressers will also stay open, though stores are only allowed 30% capacity.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/5-retailers-winning-big-during-pandemic-ecommerce-workforce-real-estate-2020-11?r=gd-sub\">5 retailers not named Amazon or Walmart that have quietly flourished during the pandemic by growing e-commerce, staff size, and total store footprint</a></em></p><p>Colleges and high schools must end all in-person teaching, but elementary and middle schools will remain open with strict safety measures, such as wearing masks, pending discussions with local authorities. Michigan hasn't seen many outbreaks connected to elementary and middle schools, state officials said, and these children are most in need of in-person teaching.</p><p>On November 10, the state recorded 57 COVID-19 deaths ‚Äì the highest daily total since early May. Its mid-November death rate is four times higher than it was in early October.</p><p>\"If we don't act now, thousands more will die, and our hospitals will continue to be overwhelmed,\" Governor Gretchen Whitmer said.</p><p>\"As hard as it is, not seeing them this Thanksgiving, imagine how much harder it would be if you couldn't see them for a future holiday ever again,\" <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-11-16/michigan-to-impose-a-three-week-partial-lockdown-to-fight-virus?sref=lAVQtUwz\">she said at a press conference.</a></p><p>Soon after Whitmer made her remarks, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-tweets-rise-up-against-michigan-coronavirus-restrictions-2020-11\">White House COVID-19 advisor Scott Atlas reacted</a> by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SWAtlasHoover/status/1328120887128842240?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1328120887128842240%7Ctwgr%5E&ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.foxnews.com%2Fus%2Ftrump-adviser-encourages-citizens-to-rise-up-against-michigan-covidovid\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"8a1cbab0426bbe951697e212e85803c6\">tweeting</a>: \"The only way this stops is if people rise up.\"&#160;</p><p>He later said he was not urging violence.</p><h2>Washington's new restrictions</h2><p>Governor Jay Inslee announced Washington's four-week partial lockdown <a href=\"https://www.governor.wa.gov/news-media/inslee-announces-statewide-restrictions-four-weeks\">Sunday</a> as cases continue to rise in the state. Over the weekend, Washington reported more than 2,000 cases a day, and average cases in the state have doubled over the past two weeks.</p><p>\"This spike puts us in a more dangerous a position as we were in March,\" Inslee said during a press conference Sunday.</p><p>\"And it means, unfortunately, the time has come to reinstate restrictions on activities statewide to preserve the public's well-being, and to save lives.\"</p><p>From Tuesday, gyms across the state will have to shut and outdoor fitness classes will face restrictions.</p><p>Leisure and entertainment facilities such as bowling alleys, movie theaters, and museums will have to close.</p><p>Stores will remain open, but only at 25% capacity.</p><p>Outdoor social gatherings will be limited to six people from different households, and indoor gatherings with people from different households are only allowed if they quarantine for fourteen days, or receive a negative COVID-19 test result within 48 hours of the gathering.</p><p>From Wednesday, restaurants and bars will also no longer be able to offer dine-in services. Diners can eat outside, but only five are allowed per table.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Futures on the S&#38;P 500 and the Dow Jones rise towards intraday highs, after drugmaker Moderna says its COVID-19 trial vaccine proved to be 94.5% effective.</li>\n<li>Crude oil futures rally by more than 3%, while technology stocks and gold fell and Treasury yields held steady.&#160;</li>\n<li>Moderna said its product&#160;can be stored for a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>US stock futures jumped on Monday, after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/moderna-coronavirus-vaccine-works-to-prevent-covid-19-company-says-2020-11?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">drugmaker Moderna</a> said its COVID-19 vaccine candidate had achieved 94.5% efficacy, solidifying optimism that a means of controlling the virus may soon be in hand.&#160;</p><p>The finding comes from a 30,000-person study that compared volunteers who got a two-dose regimen of Moderna's shot to ones who got a placebo. The vaccine was shown to be 94.5% effective in a preliminary analysis.</p><p>Futures on the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/futures/s&p-500-futuresures\">S&#38;P 500</a> and the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/futures/dow-futures\">Dow Jones</a> rose by 1.4-1.8% to trade around session highs, while those on the technology-heavy <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/futures/nasdaq-100-futures\">Nasdaq 100</a>, which contains many of the beneficiaries of the work-from-home economy that the pandemic created, surrendered initial gains and fell 0.1%</p><p>Small-cap stocks looked set for a bigger jump at the start of regular trade later. Futures on the Russell 2000 index were last up 2.6%. Many of these are highly exposed to the underlying economy and could profit first from the roll-out of an effective vaccine.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/moderna-stock-price-independent-board-covid19-vaccine-95-effective-2020-11-1029805601\">Moderna shares</a> traded as much as 9% higher in pre-market trading, while those in healthcare rivals <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pfe-stock\">Pfizer</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/astrazeneca-stock\">AstraZeneca</a> fell 1-1.8%. Shares in Johnson &#38; Johnson rose around 1.4% in premarket trading.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-cheap-companies-value-economic-rebound-goldman-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GOLDMAN SACHS: Buy these 20 deeply underpriced stocks now before the recovery helps them rebound and crush Wall Street's low expectations in 2021</a></em></p><p>Moderna's vaccine has one crucial advantage over Pfizer's shot. It can be stored for a month at typical fridge temperatures (36 degrees Fahrenheit to 46 degrees Fahrenheit), while Pfizer's shot needs to be stored at -94 degrees Fahrenheit, requiring dry ice and special containers.</p><p>\"Vaccine-related headlines will dominate the news cycle between now and year-end. Positive news should be supportive for risk appetite (so, by extension, USD negative),\" BMO Capital Markets head of European FX strategy Stephen Gallo said in a note.&#160;</p><p>The dollar fell broadly, most notably against emerging-market currencies, following the news.&#160;</p><p>Global equities have been on a tear since <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">Pfizer's announcement last Monday</a> that its vaccine had succeeded in the final stages of its clinical trial and had proven to be effective in 90% of cases. The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a> has hit record highs, while Tokyo's <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/nikkei_225\">Nikkei</a> has risen to its highest in almost 30 years.</p><p>Crude oil extended gains. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price\">Brent crude futures</a> were last up 3.5% at $44.28 a barrel, while <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/oil-price?type=wti\">WTI futures</a> rose by 3.9% to trade around $41.70 a barrel.&#160;</p><p>Meanwhile, perceived safe-havens such as US Treasuries and gold came under pressure.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/gold-price\">Gold</a> dropped by 0.9% to $1,870.35 an ounce, near the lows of the day, while the yield on the benchmark 10-year Treasury was unchanged around 0.887%.</p><p><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\">Read more:</em></strong><em data-stringify-type=\"italic\"> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-tips-for-success-william-danoff-shares-market-beating-guide-2020-11\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Peter Lynch disciple William Danoff manages over $124 billion and has beaten the market for 30 years. src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb270a3402d49001924f10b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"lavanna rivers wide\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Travel nurse Lawanna Rivers describing the COVID-19 crisis at the University Medical Center of El Paso on Facebook Live.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/lawanna.rivers/videos/3823813547631107/?t=0\" target=\"_blank\">Facebook</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Travel nurse Lawanna Rivers recently recorded a <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/lawanna.rivers/videos/3823813547631107/?t=0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Facebook Live</a> video, where she described her experience treating COVID-19 patients at the University Medical Center of El Paso.</li>\n<li>The city has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/el-paso-mayor-dee-margo-discusses-surge-in-covid-19-2020-11\">emerged as a new hotspot</a> of the virus, as the nation battles a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-surge-is-tsunami-comparison-spring-summer-2020-11\">third wave of the outbreak</a>.&#160;</li>\n<li>In the video, Rivers said the hospital's sickest COVID-19 patients were put in a \"pit\" that doctors don't&#160;enter for fear of exposing themselves to the virus.</li>\n<li>\"My first day at orientation, I was told that whatever patients go into the pit, they only come out in a body bag,\" she said, adding that this posting has been her worst during the pandemic.</li>\n<li>The hospital told <a href=\"https://kfoxtv.com/news/local/travel-nurse-accuses-umc-of-not-aggressively-treating-covid-19-patients-leading-to-deaths\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">KFOX 14</a>&#160;it \"cannot fully verify the events expressed\" in Rivers' video but acknowledged the \"difficult, physical and emotional toll\" the pandemic has taken on health workers.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A travel nurse has described the \"horrific\" scene at one hospital in El Paso, Texas, a city that has emerged as a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/el-paso-mayor-dee-margo-discusses-surge-in-covid-19-2020-11\">new hotspot</a> as the weathers its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-third-coronavirus-surge-is-tsunami-comparison-spring-summer-2020-11\">third and likely deadliest wave</a> of the coronavirus.</p><p>In a nearly hourlong <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/lawanna.rivers/videos/3823813547631107/?t=0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Facebook Live</a> video published last Saturday, Lawanna Rivers said that she had served five postings at various hospitals during the COVID-19 pandemic, but her time at the University Medical Center of El Paso was by far the worst.&#160;</p><p>\"Out of all the COVID assignments I've been on, this one here has really left me emotionally scarred,\" she said. \"The facility I'm at has surpassed the one I was at in New York.\" New York was the epicenter of the US outbreak in the spring.</p><p>Rivers was most upset about how the sickest patients at the hospital were treated. She said they were all put into an area called a \"pit,\" where they are essentially left to die.&#160;</p><p>\"My first day at orientation, I was told that whatever patients go into the pit, they only come out in a body bag,\" Rivers said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb27119402d49001924f10c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"covid test\" height=\"1335\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A nurse enters a tent for coronavirus patients at the University Medical Center of El Paso on October 30, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/nurse-enters-a-tent-for-coronavirus-patients-setup-at-news-photo/1229367969?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Cengiz Yar/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Rivers said doctors at the hospital would not enter the area, and nurses like herself who were stationed in them were under orders to perform CPR just three times on a patient before letting them die.&#160;</p><p>Rivers said she learned that doctors wouldn't enter the pit when she called a physician for help one day with a patient who was bleeding profusely. She said the doctor told her they don't go into the rooms for the sickest COVID-19 patients, so as to not expose themselves to the disease.</p><p>In the three-and-a-half weeks that she was at the hospital, Rivers said she never once saw a doctor go into a COVID-19 pit.</p><p>\"The doctors don't even step foot in those COVID rooms to see those patients ...We as nurses, it's OK for us to be exposed, but you as doctors, you don't even come in there. You can't get exposed, but we can and y'all are making all the money,\" she said.&#160;</p><p>Rivers said that she volunteered to work in a pit every day, hoping that continuity of care would help her patients get better ‚Äî but that it didn't matter because they were too sick by that point.&#160;</p><p>Rivers said she believes that if the patients had received better care earlier on, it may have made a difference.&#160;</p><p>\"I have never experienced, and have no words, for what I just experienced in El Paso, Texas,\" she said. \"If those doctors there would aggressively treat those patients from the beginning, a lot more would make it.\"</p><p>Rivers also accused the hospital of giving special treatment to the wife of a doctor once. She said this woman, whom a nurse at one point called a \"VIP\" patient, was the only person to make it out of the ICU alive during her nearly a month at the hospital.&#160;</p><p>\"They pulled out all the stops for that woman, it was nothing that they didn't do for that woman. And guess what? She was the one patient that made it out of the ICU alive, and was able to downgrade to a longterm acute care. So you mean to tell me because she's a doctor's wife, her life meant more than any of those other patients?\"</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fb2719d1c741f0019ac9eb8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"university medical center el paso\" height=\"1007\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The University Medical Center of El Paso.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Google Street View</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>In another shocking testimony, Rivers described how a worker once wheeled in a dead body into her unit because the morgue was full.</p><p>\"The morgue was so full of bodies that they had ran out of room, so once the doors opened to the pit they come wheeling in a body already in a bag,\" she said.</p><p>\"Lined 'em up with the rest of our alive patients, because they had to store the body in there, because the morgue was out of room. They've had to bring in freezer trucks because there's so many bodies.\"</p><p>Rivers said that she left her assignment in El Paso early because she couldn't bear to watch more patients die.</p><p>\"I've seen so many deaths in this last month, than I've seen in my entire 13-year career,\" Rivers said.</p><p>She said she was also afraid for her life, and the kind of care she would receive if she got sick there.&#160;</p><p>\"I kept saying: 'I can't get sick here in Texas, because if I get COVID here in Texas ... I'm going to die. It was that bad,\" she said.</p><p>Business Insider has contacted the University Medical Center of El Paso for comment.</p><p>The hospital has been releasing the same statement to local outlets about Rivers' video.</p><p>\"After watching the video, while we cannot fully verify the events expressed, we empathize and sympathize with the difficult, physical and emotional toll that this pandemic takes on thousands of healthcare workers here and throughout our country,\" hospital spokesman Ryan Mielke said in the statement, according to <a href=\"https://kfoxtv.com/news/local/travel-nurse-accuses-umc-of-not-aggressively-treating-covid-19-patients-leading-to-deaths\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">KFOX 14.</a></p><p>\"This particular travel nurse was at UMC briefly to help El Paso confront the surge of COVID-19 patients.\"</p><p>Watch Rivers' full 50-minute Facebook Live video below:&#160;</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe src=\"https://www.facebook.com/plugins/video.php?href=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2Flawanna.rivers%2Fvideos%2F3823813547631107%2F&show_text=0&width=267\" width=\"267\" height=\"476\" style=\"border:none;overflow:hidden\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" allow=\"autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; picture-in-picture; web-share\" allowfullscreen=\"true\"></iframe></div><p>Texas currently has the most coronavirus cases in the US, <a href=\"https://www.worldometers.info/coronavirus/country/us/\">according to Worldometer</a>, and El Paso county has the third-most infections in the state, according to the <a href=\"https://txdshs.maps.arcgis.com/apps/opsdashboard/index.html#/ed483ecd702b4298ab01e8b9cafc8b83\">Texas health department</a>.</p><p>Earlier this month the county <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/el-paso-doubles-mobile-morgue-capacity-new-coronavirus-surge-2020-11\">doubled its number of mobile morgues</a> ‚Äî which are typically refrigerated trucks ‚Äî to store COVID-19 victims' bodies, and <a href=\"https://kfoxtv.com/news/coronavirus/el-paso-moves-to-10-mobile-morgues-for-covid-19-deaths-as-judge-wants-to-extend-shutdown\">KFOX 14 reported</a> that patients were dying at such a rate that medical examiners have not been able to keep up.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/D8UC9deS5C8\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 16 Nov 2020 14:24:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fad37d17f8f4200182a675b?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"d2678359020b1ae946ce485eda54159a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn81@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-20-158_7adca710b4b89953.webp","destWidth":3858,"destHeight":2893,"sourceBytes":186578,"destBytes":186578,"author":"insider@insider.com (Business Insider)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f90840d212113001873ffab?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn27@2020_3/2020/11/16/16-46-27-956_80a7cdb3e2c36574.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-27-479_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=D8UC9deS5C8:t7Sd4buTHhQ:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-28-068_515f660a4315627e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=D8UC9deS5C8:t7Sd4buTHhQ:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn12@2020_6/2020/11/16/16-46-22-649_b9310c39b0c15962.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-24-391_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=D8UC9deS5C8:t7Sd4buTHhQ:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn59@2020_4/2020/11/16/16-46-23-098_f56aa98d39d5339a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/D8UC9deS5C8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn27@2020_1/2020/11/16/16-46-21-936_94e1efcf45b6410e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605545138312},{"createdTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","updatedTime":"2020-11-17 00:45:38","title":"How to enable two-factor authentication on Apple devices to keep your data secure","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/two-factor-authentication-apple","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeef031c741f0019ac9c5e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman holding cell phone with laptop computer open\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Two-factor authentication is an important step to take to secure all your accounts.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Cavan Images/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Apple's two-factor authentication feature provides extra security for users' personal account information.</li>\n<li>Set-up of two-factor authentication differs depending on whether you're using an iPhone, iPad, or a Mac computer.</li>\n<li>You can turn off two-factor authentication at any time if you no longer wish to use it.</li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">Visit Business Insider's Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Ensuring your personal information remains private and secure when you're online is a top priority for most people, and one of the easiest ways to protect sensitive data is by enabling <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/two-factor-authentication\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">two-factor authentication</a> on your apps and devices. If you're an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/apple\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Apple</a> user, doing this is a simple process that will guarantee only you have access to your account.&#160;</p><p>It should be noted that setup of two-factor authentication differs depending on whether you're using a mobile device such as an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/iphone\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">iPhone</a> or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/ipad\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">iPad</a> or if you're on a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/mac\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mac</a> computer. However, once enabled, you'll need to enter not just your password but also a six-digit code sent to your trusted device every time you want to log into your account.&#160;</p><h2>How to enable two-factor authentication on Apple devices</h2><h3>On an iPhone or iPad:&#160;</h3><p><strong>1.</strong> First, ensure your device is updated to at least iOS 10.3 before beginning. Then, tap the Settings icon on your device's home screen.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> Tap your name at the top of the Settings menu, then tap \"Password &#38; Security.\" You may need to enter your iCloud password.</p><p><strong>3.</strong> Next, enter and verify a new trusted phone number. This should be either the number of your device if you're using an iPhone or your phone number on whatever phone you do use.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeeb751c741f0019ac9c39?format=jpeg\" alt=\"two_factor_authentication_2\" height=\"2208\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Enter your phone number, choose &#34;Text message&#34; or &#34;Phone call,&#34; and hit &#34;Send.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jennifer Still/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>4.</strong> Hit \"Send,\" which will prompt Apple to send a message to your phone number containing a six-digit code.&#160;</p><p><strong>5.</strong> Enter the code in the box where prompted, which will turn on two-factor authentication.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5faeebe9402d49001924eea7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"two factor_authentication_1__1_\" height=\"1964\" width=\"1242\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Two-factor authentication should now be turned on.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jennifer Still/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3>On a Mac:&#160;</h3><p><strong>1.</strong> Ensure your Mac is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-update-mac\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">upgraded to the most recent operating system.</a>&#160;Then click the Apple menu and open System Preferences.&#160;</p><p><strong>2.</strong> Click \"Apple ID\" and then open \"Password &#38; Security\" by double-clicking.&#160;</p><p><strong>3.</strong> Click \"Turn on two-factor authentication.\" Your ID will then be protected.&#160;</p><p>It should be noted that if you created your Apple ID in iOS 10.3 or macOS 10.12.4 or later, two-step authentication is automatically turned on and you won't need to follow the steps above. In addition, should you ever decide you no longer want to use the feature, it can be disabled at any time.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 100%\"><iframe src=\"https://produktor.businessinsider.com/productCardService?id=5d8e19fb2e22af18f40d281d&type=small&live=true\" width=\"100%\" height=\"150%\" frameborder=\"0\"
